type=\"hidden\" value=\"mnras\" /> \n    </div>\n\r\n                    </div>\r\n                </div>\r\n            </div>\r\n            <div id=\"ContentTab\" class=\"content active\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=26154430 id=\"26154430\" class=\"abstract-title\" >Abstract</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We present a detailed analysis of an individual case of gravitational lensing of a <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 Lyman-break galaxy (LBG) in a blank field, identified in <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> imaging obtained as part of the Brightest of Reionizing Galaxies survey. To investigate the close proximity of the bright (<em>m</em><sub><em>AB</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a025.8) <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>-dropout to a small group of foreground galaxies, we obtained deep spectroscopy of the dropout and two foreground galaxies using VLT/X-Shooter. We detect H\u00a0\u03b1, H\u00a0\u03b2, [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] emission in the brightest two foreground galaxies (unresolved at the natural seeing of 0.8\u00a0arcsec), placing the pair at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327. We can rule out emission lines contributing all of the observed broad-band flux in <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> band at 70\u03c3, allowing us to exclude the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 candidate as a low-redshift interloper with broad-band photometry dominated by strong emission lines. The foreground galaxy pair lies at the peak of the luminosity, redshift and separation distributions for deflectors of strongly lensed <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 objects, and we make a marginal detection of a demagnified secondary image in the deepest (<em>J</em><sub>125</sub>) filter. We show that the configuration can be accurately modelled by a singular isothermal ellipsoidal deflector and a S\u00e9rsic source magnified by a factor of \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a04.3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2. The reconstructed source in the best-fitting model is consistent with luminosities and morphologies of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBGs in the literature. The lens model yields a group mass of 9.62\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.31\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>11</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub> and a stellar mass-to-light ratio for the brightest deflector galaxy of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$M_{\\star }/L_{B}=2.3^{+0.8}_{-0.6} \\,\\mathrm{M}_{{\\odot }}/\\mathrm{L}_{{\\odot }}$|</span> within its effective radius. The foreground galaxies\u2019 redshifts would make this one of the few strong lensing deflectors discovered at <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a01. Deeper imaging would allow for confirmation of the existence of the secondary image and elongation in the primary image, verifying multiple imaging and producing more robust estimations of the image magnifications.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: high-redshift&quot;\">galaxies: high-redshift</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;cosmology: observations&quot;\">cosmology: observations</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=26154432 id=\"26154432\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The epoch of reionization at redshift <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a07\u201312 (Komatsu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib39\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib39\" data-open=\"bib39\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Shull et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib61\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib61\" data-open=\"bib61\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Planck Collaboration I <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib53\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib53\" data-open=\"bib53\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) is a key period in the evolution of the Universe when the first galaxies formed and reionized the neutral hydrogen in the intergalactic medium. Due to the absorption of emitted photons with energies high enough to ionize neutral hydrogen, the spectra of these early galaxies have highly attenuated regions bluer than the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 break at 1216\u2009\u00c5, enabling their identification from broad-band imaging with the Lyman-break, or \u2018dropout\u2019, technique (Steidel et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib64\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib64\" data-open=\"bib64\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>; Giavalisco <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>). This technique has been used successfully to build large galaxy samples out to <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08, with sources selected using observations from both ground- and space-based observatories (e.g. Bradley et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; McLure et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib41\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib41\" data-open=\"bib41\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Finkelstein et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Schmidt et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib58\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib58\" data-open=\"bib58\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Bouwens et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">These new observations have opened the possibility of quantifying and studying the galaxy luminosity function during the epoch of reionization as well as its evolution with redshift (Khochfar et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Bouwens et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Castellano et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Trenti et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib66\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib66\" data-open=\"bib66\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Bradley et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Finkelstein et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Oesch et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib49\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib49\" data-open=\"bib49\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; McLure et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib41\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib41\" data-open=\"bib41\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Robertson et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib54\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib54\" data-open=\"bib54\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib55\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib55\" data-open=\"bib55\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Schenker et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib57\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib57\" data-open=\"bib57\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Finkelstein et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Schmidt et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib58\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib58\" data-open=\"bib58\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Measurement of the luminosity function is a key requirement for understanding the production of ionizing photons at high redshift, which completes hydrogen reionization. In this context, it is of fundamental importance to discriminate between intrinsic evolution of the galaxy luminosity function and observational selection effects.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">One possible effect is gravitational lensing magnification bias (e.g. Wallington &amp; Narayan <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib77\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib77\" data-open=\"bib77\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1993</a>). While the fraction of random lines of sight at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a06 that are strongly gravitationally lensed by massive foreground galaxies is around \u223c0.5\u00a0per\u00a0cent (Barkana &amp; Loeb <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>; Comerford, Haiman &amp; Schaye <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Wyithe et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib82\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib82\" data-open=\"bib82\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Mason et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), the steep nature of the high-redshift luminosity function results in observationally bright Lyman-break galaxies (LBGs) having an excess likelihood of having been gravitationally lensed (Wyithe et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib82\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib82\" data-open=\"bib82\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Fialkov &amp; Loeb <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). In general, magnification bias depends on the slope of the luminosity function of the source galaxies: steeper luminosity functions yield more lensed sources because the loss in solid angle is compensated by the steep rise in number counts at deeper flux limits. Therefore, this effect becomes especially important for the bright end of the galaxy luminosity function (<em>L</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a0<em>L</em><sub>\u22c6</sub>), where <em>L</em><sub>\u22c6</sub> is the \u2018knee\u2019 of the luminosity function in the Schechter parametrization, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\phi (L){\\rm d}L = \\phi _{\\star }(L/L_{\\star })^{\\alpha } \\exp ^{-(L/L_{\\star })}{\\rm d}(L/L_{\\star })$|\u2060</span>. In Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), we showed that magnification bias exists in LBG surveys at\u00a0\u22734, and becomes a significant factor in surveys of LBGs at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a07, with \u223c10\u00a0per\u00a0cent of LBGs brighter than <em>L</em><sub>\u22c6</sub> strongly lensed in fields without massive structures such as the Hubble eXtreme Deep Field (XDF; Illingworth et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>), and Cosmic Assembly Near-infrared Deep Extragalactic Legacy Survey fields (CANDELS; Grogin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib32\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib32\" data-open=\"bib32\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Koekemoer et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib38\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib38\" data-open=\"bib38\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The results in Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) confirm the prediction of Wyithe et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib82\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib82\" data-open=\"bib82\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>) that \u223c10\u00a0per\u00a0cent of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBGs in a survey with a flux limit around <em>M</em><sub>\u22c6</sub>, such as the Brightest of Reionizing Galaxies (BoRG) WFC3 <em>HST</em> survey (Trenti et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib68\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib68\" data-open=\"bib68\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Bradley et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), could be strongly lensed. Hence the BoRG survey offers the perfect data set to extend the findings of Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). In fact, an analysis of the BoRG survey by Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) found that 3\u201315\u00a0per\u00a0cent of LBGs in the BoRG fields are expected to be strongly lensed, depending on the specific flux limit of each field. They also investigated individual <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 candidates in the BoRG survey and found one good candidate for strong gravitational lensing, having an estimated magnification of \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a02.02\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.52. They also identified a further three candidates with lower magnifications of \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a01.80\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.33, 1.54\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.62 and 1.47\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.30.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The relatively small number of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 candidates in the BoRG survey do not allow a statistical approach, such as that undertaken by Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), to detect evidence of gravitational lensing. In this paper, we adopt a direct approach to search for evidence of gravitational lensing by looking at individual LBGs. We only consider the highest signal-to-noise (S/N) LBGs in the BoRG sample, which includes 10 candidates detected at S/N\u00a0\u2265\u00a08\u03c3 and <em>m</em>\u00a0\u2272\u00a027 (\u2248<em>M</em><sub>\u22c6</sub> at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08). The results from Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) and Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) imply that \u22481 of these LBGs should be strongly gravitationally lensed. We inspected these 10 LBGs searching for potential gravitationally lensed configurations, and find one <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 candidate in close projection to a foreground group of galaxies.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This paper is structured as follows. We discuss the data, photometry and spectroscopy in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a>, we introduce the Markov-Chain Monte Carlo (MCMC) method that we have applied to investigate the lensing hypothesis, as well as the MCMC results. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>, we compare the inferred <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 source properties to those in the literature. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>, we investigate the properties of the deflector. We discuss the evidence for lensing in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec6\"></span><a href=\"#sec6\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">6</a>, and we conclude in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec7\"></span><a href=\"#sec7\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">7</a>. Throughout this paper we assume a \u039bCDM cosmology of \u03a9<sub>M</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.27, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.73 and <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a070kms<sup>\u22121</sup>Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>. We quote magnitudes in the AB system (Oke &amp; Gunn <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib51\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib51\" data-open=\"bib51\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1983</a>). We refer to the <em>F</em>600<em>LP</em>, <em>F</em>098<em>M</em>, <em>F</em>125<em>W</em> and <em>F</em>160<em>W</em><em>HST</em> filters as <em>V</em><sub>600</sub>, <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>, <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=26154439 id=\"26154439\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 THE SEARCH FOR STRONG GRAVITATIONAL LENSING IN THE BRIGHTEST OF REIONIZING GALAXIES SURVEY</h2>\r\n                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154440 id=\"26154440\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-1>2.1 The BoRG survey</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The BoRG survey is a Hubble Wide-Field Camera 3 (WFC3) large, multiyear pure-parallel programme aimed at identifying galaxy candidates at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a07.5 from their colours based on the Lyman-break technique (Steidel et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib64\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib64\" data-open=\"bib64\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>). Until recently, the main focus of BoRG has been identification of galaxies at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 as <em>Y</em>-band dropouts, while ongoing observations (cycle 22; #13767; PI Trenti) are optimized for selecting <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08\u20139 candidates.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In this work, we use data from observations acquired before cycle 22. The core of this earlier data set is based on WFC3 imaging in four filters (<em>V</em><sub>606</sub>, <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>, <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>, <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>) obtained as part of <em>HST</em> programmes #11700 and #12572 (PI Trenti), complemented by archival data with a similar observational design and the same infrared filters, but with <em>F</em>600<em>LP</em> substituting <em>F</em>606<em>W</em> (<em>HST</em> program #11702, PI Yan; Yan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib83\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib83\" data-open=\"bib83\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). A full description of the survey and of its findings is reported by Trenti et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib67\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib67\" data-open=\"bib67\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib68\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib68\" data-open=\"bib68\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), Bradley et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) and Schmidt et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib58\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib58\" data-open=\"bib58\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). To summarize, the last comprehensive data release of the BoRG survey yielded <em>n</em>\u00a0=\u00a038 <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG candidates identified as <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>-dropouts with <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> magnitudes between 25.5 and 27.6\u00a0mag (Schmidt et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib58\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib58\" data-open=\"bib58\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). These candidates were obtained by analysing data over a total area of 350\u00a0arcmin<sup>2</sup> divided in 71 independent lines of sight.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154443 id=\"26154443\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-2>2.2 Search for a candidate strongly lensed <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The large number of independent fields in BoRG results in a sample essentially unaffected by large-scale structure uncertainty (Trenti &amp; Stiavelli <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>), and includes a variety of different environments in terms of line-of-sight structure, representing an ideal data set to quantify magnification bias in a different manner to that used by Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) and Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). To search for evidence of large magnifications, we have visually inspected the regions surrounding the 10 sources detected with an S/N\u00a0\u2265\u00a08\u03c3 in the BoRG survey, all of which have <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{J_{125}}\\leq 27.0$|</span> searching for evidence of strong gravitational lensing. We investigate only the highest S/N objects because they offer the best chance of identifying direct evidence of strong lensing in the event that they have been significantly magnified. Indications of strong gravitational lensing that we inspect for are proximity of the dropout to bright foreground objects, and secondary images with similar colours to the dropout. Cutouts of the 10 candidates in the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band are shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"26154445\" scrollto-destination=\"26154445\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig1.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=uPvrR2OaB5cDyIThE~GtljZZ-vunCVv25BwaDKjJdnxUEL17aI8kq45bI6IJ4ZIqeTC7UwfnoGTz4H~MwnnOhBn0vSON2gKUgk6MG18xJZfnZUzgQd7PLwU-zI1uUvCMmq6Hu1ZMvUgXp9WRgFvD0H~MVbWA4EcL6bW5Psreud69XFLbRZ~p52AEw0g5FWkA2jRMSAdZFWhzjrN6uKv3125GEA7c3UzI37WIgbvvAIcNcN9SpJYpxf~a52J54yebtvh6bA9BjSpGBTlxyvP4mhOrfT~7BIp2UFBL0mFqeME~nrTah9yRGHZxAaolQLYFgiRD4BOIYV~MwDzQgxOSKQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The 10 8\u03c3 z\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG candidates identified in the BoRG survey. Seven of the 10 candidates are ruled out as being strongly gravitationally lensed due to the absence of foreground objects along the line of sight. Seven of the 10 candidates are ruled out as being strongly gravitationally lensed due to the absence of foreground objects along the line of sight. The object borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_1301$|</span>+<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$0000\\_160$|</span> appears nearby a bright foreground galaxy, and Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) assess its magnification to be \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a01.47\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.30. The object borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_1437$|</span>+<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5043\\_1137$|</span> appears 2.6\u00a0arcsec from a bright foreground at <em>z</em><sub>phot</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.4. Using the framework of Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), this object has a magnification of \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a01.3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2 and a 5\u00a0per\u00a0cent chance of being strongly lensed. Neither of these configurations display obvious secondary images, which is the key criterion for constraining strong lensing. The object borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_682$|</span> is in close proximity to a group of three foreground galaxies, around which a candidate secondary image is identified.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">We identify one good candidate for a strongly gravitationally lensed <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG (borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_682$|</span> in the notation of Bradley et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), which appears very close in projection to a compact grouping of three foreground galaxies (borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_647$|\u2060</span>, which consists of two objects, and borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_650$|\u2060</span>). Through visual inspection of the configuration, we identify a possible faint (S/N\u00a0\u223c\u00a02) counter image, which appears in the deepest band, <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>, and is located immediately below the foreground galaxies opposite the location of the dropout. The location and flux relative to the brighter image is consistent with gravitational lensing theory, which predicts secondary images to appear demagnified on the opposite side of the deflector, and at a smaller separation from the deflector than the brighter image. In fact, a strikingly similar gravitational lensing configuration has been observed (Wong et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib80\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib80\" data-open=\"bib80\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>, see fig. 3) with almost identical relative image positions, magnifications and flux ratio, albeit with a lower redshift source and smaller deflection angles.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The proximity to multiple bright foreground galaxies and identification of a possible secondary image with similar colours to the dropout makes <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\rm borg}\\_0440\\_5244\\_682$|</span> a good candidate to be significantly magnified, warranting further investigation. Postage-stamp images of the dropout and foreground galaxies in the single optical and three near-IR filters of the BoRG survey are presented in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>, where the objects are labelled in the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> panel.</p>                        <a id=\"26154448\" scrollto-destination=\"26154448\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig2.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=WYOng0IG21t894YfyqbcN40Ih06nj0X573y8us-vi2Ol~bj16Dkmc8GMb5YcSDMJBUBYH3CcsHR-iTzYiSBw2iwwgnlhUMhJjXCFZi4COHS4TwENN4t3crCyWQrMCuDH6BIMrEBFRQQaH9zAE9eRiGPPNnGBzfFXQur1ooWJ81fYuQ71zIIR6RqS9LPzVYLmvCKjcVj-2~5KEkpwbKsEK-JEkAvZ6lC2dTdxvIbW0Wb3sP184blPlWq7nUzK3QaGbmDtmnF1PW5xEKSKWcHgAT~zS8pM7C-Y8-7t6j1VEhZQSP1izrsyPmX-DKXKfzif4RUL49FuiWV6giduU19jfQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Postage stamp images of the candidate lensed z\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 galaxy in field BoRG$\\_0440$-5244 in the four HST/WFC3 filters (left to right: V600, Y098, J125, H160). The images are 5.0\u00a0arcsec on each side. All cutouts are shown on the same scale.</p></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154449 id=\"26154449\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-3>2.3 Photometry of the dropout and foreground objects</h3>\r\n<div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">The candidate <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 galaxy, borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_682$|\u2060</span>, was identified in field borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-5244 (following the notation of Bradley et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). Identification of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 dropouts is made according to strict colour selection. In general, <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a07.5 galaxies are identified due to a strong break between the <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> and <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> filters, a blue or flat <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> \u2212 <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> colour and a non-detection in the optical <em>V</em><sub>600</sub> band. The selection criteria requires, <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"\" content-id=\"\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray*}\r\n&amp;&amp;{{\\rm S/N}_{V_{600}} &lt; 1.5}\\nonumber \\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{(Y_{098} - J_{125}) &gt; 1.75}\\nonumber \\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{(J_{125} - H_{160}) &lt; 0.02 + 0.15[(Y_{098} - J_{125}) - 1.75]}\\nonumber .\r\n\\end{eqnarray*} </div></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The conservative non-detection limit of 1.5\u03c3 in the <em>V</em><sub>600</sub> filter is crucial in producing a clean <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 sample (Bouwens et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). The photometry presented by Bradley et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) of the candidates analysed here gives a <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> magnitude of 25.9\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1\u00a0mag, a <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> residual of &gt;2.1\u00a0mag, and S/N after sky subtraction in <em>V</em><sub>600</sub>, <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>, <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> of \u22120.8, \u22120.5, 9.1 and 5.7, respectively. We find a <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> ellipticity for the dropout of \u03f5\u00a0=\u00a00.4\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1 tangential to the direction of the largest of the proposed lensing galaxies. The <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> half-light radius of the dropout was measured, using SE<span class=\"small-caps\">xtractor</span>, to be 0.21\u00a0arcsec (1.1\u00a0kpc at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08; not corrected for PSF broadening).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The two brighter foreground objects are identified as a single blended source (borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_647$|\u2060</span>) with <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{J_{125}}=23.41\\pm 0.02$|</span>\u00a0mag in the BoRG SE<span class=\"small-caps\">xtractor</span> catalogue. We performed fixed aperture photometry on the individual galaxies of borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_647$|</span> and found the brighter galaxy to be 1.3\u20131.5\u00a0mag brighter than the fainter galaxy in each of the filters, making the colours of the two galaxies essentially identical colours. The galaxy borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_650$|\u2060</span>, has <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{J_{125}}\\sim 24.58\\pm 0.14$|</span>\u00a0mag. The photometry of all objects is summarized in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"26154453\" scrollto-destination=\"26154453\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The photometry for the primary dropout (ID: 682), the main lensing group (ID: 647) and a nearby galaxy (ID: 650) which is potentially part of the group. The main lensing group (647) has a spectroscopically confirmed redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327. The photometric redshift probability distribution of the third object (650) is extended; however, it has a non-negligible probability of residing at the same redshift as the central galaxies.</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table><thead><tr><th>ID<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>V</em><sub>600</sub><span class=\"table-modal\"><table><thead><tr><th>ID<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>V</em><sub>600</sub><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>Y</em><sub>098</sub><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>J</em><sub>125</sub><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>H</em><sub>160</sub><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>682\u00a0</td><td>&gt;28.26\u00a0</td><td>&gt;28.15\u00a0</td><td>25.92\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.14\u00a0</td><td>25.75\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.19\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>647\u00a0</td><td>24.20\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.07\u00a0</td><td>23.87\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03\u00a0</td><td>23.41\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02\u00a0</td><td>23.49\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>650\u00a0</td><td>25.17\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.13\u00a0</td><td>24.87\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.05\u00a0</td><td>24.58\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.14\u00a0</td><td>24.31\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.31\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/26154453\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154454 id=\"26154454\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-4>2.4 Photometry of the candidate counter image</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In addition to the photometry already carried out by Bradley et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), we perform aperture photometry in <span class=\"small-caps\">iraf</span> on the primary and counter image to determine their flux ratio and the counter image's <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>V</em><sub>606</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> colours. To minimize contamination of the counter image photometry by the lensing group, we operate on a version of the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> images where we subtracted a scaled and PSF-matched version of the <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> data, where the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 candidate has dropped out. For this, we use <span class=\"small-caps\">isis2.2</span> (Alard <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>) to produce a convolution kernel between the images in the different bands and to match the point spread functions (PSFs). There is some residual in the subtracted images due to the foreground galaxies having intrinsically different profiles between filters. The galaxies on the whole, though, are adequately subtracted, and the residuals do not affect the photometry at the image positions. The subtracted images are shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"26154456\" scrollto-destination=\"26154456\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig3.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=3oRe~IY7UZ7PIL~DQu9Q3UineWMa5nTfEhTR9WbIvjj0pJaruzFAqqechnn6UexcbAdP7vW-t7QTXR9nRNNfrv7GShIv0xNzoAPET1K1LefrYXvEPNC4AFOOxYuE04ADNSUfuu3Z6~R1uLzrXZDau~7Hr7I-rmoe5lRHlDDA~37wfpf4hXTvGYxFvaBCzze7zucUEC257m63DXhP070jwlPx6DF4LI4UB~-xf8ZB3zl7tIa9Y6XqqT0nNPl54NcNm2On53HAASslRjSAABrcIrmiva295y6446RpmHFLaxaLOSQXtZklLqJ5G8yTqNfi~~F1sXmBVOkNnhD9HNrgeQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Normalized residuals for the subtractions of the PSF-matched Y098 image from the J125 image (left) and H160 image (right). The images are 5.0\u00a0arcsec on each side. There remains some residual of the deflector galaxy cores due to the varying light profiles of the galaxies between filters. There is a marginal detection of the counter image (S/N\u00a0\u223c\u00a02) in <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>. As expected, the counter image is undetected in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> filter. The location of the dropout objects are circled in black.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig3.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=3oRe~IY7UZ7PIL~DQu9Q3UineWMa5nTfEhTR9WbIvjj0pJaruzFAqqechnn6UexcbAdP7vW-t7QTXR9nRNNfrv7GShIv0xNzoAPET1K1LefrYXvEPNC4AFOOxYuE04ADNSUfuu3Z6~R1uLzrXZDau~7Hr7I-rmoe5lRHlDDA~37wfpf4hXTvGYxFvaBCzze7zucUEC257m63DXhP070jwlPx6DF4LI4UB~-xf8ZB3zl7tIa9Y6XqqT0nNPl54NcNm2On53HAASslRjSAABrcIrmiva295y6446RpmHFLaxaLOSQXtZklLqJ5G8yTqNfi~~F1sXmBVOkNnhD9HNrgeQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Normalized residuals for the subtractions of the PSF-matched Y098 image from the J125 image (left) and H160 image (right). The location of the dropout objects are circled in black.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig3.tiff\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/26154456/stv1872fig3.tiff\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig3.tiff\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"26154456\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/stv1872fig3.png?Expires=1611467343&Signature=bCR60bEWdUPwMZB4OuTain2czW1U62fVrXlm73xy-1SpzXjHZKJd3jDKOhlwHXNcnVh-jowXOcW9xHE04mbI6Obx6vZmSD5dy7HwpziJhh0BP0QRLrSt9HiT0q5RlhS2Yl1BlACiYNDNZYEXK3YRxEd2q8-apGdkgaqzEa77ReK40zBd~6bm3onKfL4CBp4kv9myq7iGc3Ga1xyuS-yHpohd6Z5Fm2l3BdkCXMgRbN-9zy1NzWllRYWITQYAY5wUD8pDNdkvk2cOhUPBRzg~kW2YHUA8PWJvdNraq~zJkGizp-f4sNduDT6Pw4th6~IvpAbIMUAJ-m91UzD~S0yUug__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=26154456&ar=1752732&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig3.tiff\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Normalized residuals for the subtractions of the PSF-matched <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> image from the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> image (left) and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> image (right). The images are 5.0\u00a0arcsec on each side. There remains some residual of the deflector galaxy cores due to the varying light profiles of the galaxies between filters. There is a marginal detection of the counter image (S/N\u00a0\u223c\u00a02) in <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>. As expected, the counter image is undetected in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> filter. The location of the dropout objects are circled in black.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Photometry is performed in a 4\u00a0pixel circular aperture (0.32\u00a0arcsec). In <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>, the integrated flux in the primary image is 1.54\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.18\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221230</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup>\u00a0Hz<sup>\u22121</sup> (consistent with the S/N = 9.1 determination in Bradley et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), and the flux in the counter image is 3.21\u00a0\u00b1\u00a01.72\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221231</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup>\u00a0Hz<sup>\u22121</sup>. The uncertainty includes both Poisson noise and background. This gives a flux ratio of 4.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a02.6, where the large error propagates from the low S/N of the counter image.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We measure a <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> colour redder than 1.2\u00a0mag and a <em>V</em><sub>606</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> colour redder than 0.5\u00a0mag for the counter image. When the <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> and <em>V</em><sub>606</sub> images are stacked, the (<em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>\u00a0+\u00a0<em>V</em><sub>606</sub>) \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> colour is redder than 1.4\u00a0mag. While BoRG is not designed to detect such faint objects, and neither of these colours satisfy the formal BoRG criteria for <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG selection, the colours are consistent with both the brighter image, and the source being at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 but beyond the limiting depths of this field.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We do not detect a signal at the location of the counter image in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> image; however, this is not surprising as the flux ratio between the primary and counter image is measured in <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> to be 4.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a02.6, and the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> primary image is detected at 5.7\u03c3, hence we only expect the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> counter image to be undetected (S/N = 1.2\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.7). Inspection of the individual flat-fielded files in <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> does not suggest that the faint counter image candidate is a detector artefact.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The non-detection in <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> is taken into account in our MCMC analysis (Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a>), as both bands are fitted simultaneously.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154461 id=\"26154461\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-5>2.5 Spectroscopy of the central foreground galaxies and dropout</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The source and foreground galaxy configuration and image flux ratios outlined in the previous sections and Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> present the exciting possibility that this system is a <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 galaxy gravitationally lensed by a foreground galaxy group. In order to further strengthen this interpretation, we obtained spectroscopic observations of the foreground galaxy group and <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG candidate. The goals of the spectroscopic measurements of the system are twofold. The first goal was to obtain spectroscopic redshifts for the two foreground galaxies (ID: 647). The second goal was to either identify emission lines, such as Ly\u00a0\u03b1, at the location of the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG candidate (ID: 682), or use the lack of emission lines to constrain its redshift in conjunction with its photometric colours (e.g. Treu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib74\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib74\" data-open=\"bib74\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In order to obtain these measurements, we carried out VLT/X-Shooter spectroscopic observations in visitor mode on 2013 August 13\u201315 (program #091.A-0053, PI Puzia). Observing conditions were excellent with seeing in the range 0.6\u20130.9\u00a0arcsec. The X-Shooter long slit (11\u00a0arcsec) was positioned to cover both the central pair of foreground deflectors (ID: 647 in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>) and the Y-dropout (ID: 682). X-Shooter provides an uninterrupted wavelength coverage in the range 300\u00a0&lt;\u00a0\u03bb\u00a0&lt;\u00a02480\u2009nm, allowing us to characterize emission lines both from the deflector and the dropouts with a single observation. A total exposure time of 6\u00a0h (3\u00a0h on target) was achieved on the source. Telluric standard stars were observed for calibration purposes throughout the duration of the observations. The data were then reduced using the European Southern Observatory (ESO) X-Shooter pipeline v.2.5.2 (Modigliani et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib43\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib43\" data-open=\"bib43\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) and the Gasgano data file organizer developed by ESO.</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=26154464 id=\"26154464\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-5-1>2.5.1 Emission lines from the foreground galaxies</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We search for emission lines at the location of the two central foreground galaxies to determine their redshift. The two galaxies have a separation of 0.7\u00a0arcsec, and the seeing of the observations was 0.6\u20130.9\u00a0arcsec, therefore the two galaxies are unresolved in the spectrum. We identify the redshifted hydrogen\u00a0\u03b1 6563\u2009\u00c5, hydrogen\u00a0\u03b2 4861\u2009\u00c5, [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] 5007 and 4959\u2009\u00c5 doublet and the [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] 3726 and 3729\u2009\u00c5 doublet emission lines at the location of the two foreground galaxies. The two-dimensional spectrum of the hydrogen\u00a0\u03b1 and [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] doublet emission lines are shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>. The observed emission lines unambiguously places the foreground galaxy pair at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327, supporting the gravitational lensing hypothesis. This redshift is at the peak of the redshift distribution for the deflectors of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a07\u20138 LBGs (Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p>                        <a id=\"26154466\" scrollto-destination=\"26154466\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 4.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig4.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=w-RjYJrBjh2LxRFF8ZGJ0YIzBk5eVLwAIdWfbvuQq1BlMv3kzSR6r3H-T9n4i3OkY-dzH7hspzOqkD5IYhHbSkpavTj0dxBmKqVcqBJJv75nmA9RVTTF3xBPKka0-3Z7KiLmvM-O4R9fyYFCo~kWZBjmw0q4ZBNSypo67O9qG34EFvDozsREmF9PdY2J41gHiys3lpRk9Kn95iJkoNUDK2KyyfQPP552TGSFWUtXjDKmGMn-D60vMR2eLuPQPz3jcGmStosD-baNXjueXDlLmO9Ji-Rzrj8YWkdh4-SLik~R~9hfCOyDVVs2f~PsIA74fRSFDsk58jrxIJqsZmf6mQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The cropped two-dimensional spectrum of the central deflector galaxies, obtained using X-Shooter on the VLT. These emission lines provide a robust spectroscopic redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327 for the deflector galaxies.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 4.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig4.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=w-RjYJrBjh2LxRFF8ZGJ0YIzBk5eVLwAIdWfbvuQq1BlMv3kzSR6r3H-T9n4i3OkY-dzH7hspzOqkD5IYhHbSkpavTj0dxBmKqVcqBJJv75nmA9RVTTF3xBPKka0-3Z7KiLmvM-O4R9fyYFCo~kWZBjmw0q4ZBNSypo67O9qG34EFvDozsREmF9PdY2J41gHiys3lpRk9Kn95iJkoNUDK2KyyfQPP552TGSFWUtXjDKmGMn-D60vMR2eLuPQPz3jcGmStosD-baNXjueXDlLmO9Ji-Rzrj8YWkdh4-SLik~R~9hfCOyDVVs2f~PsIA74fRSFDsk58jrxIJqsZmf6mQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The cropped two-dimensional spectrum of the central deflector galaxies, obtained using X-Shooter on the VLT. Top: the hydrogen\u00a0\u03b1 emission line, identified at \u03bb\u00a0=\u00a015\u2009272\u2009\u00c5. Bottom: The [O\u00a0iii] doublet emission lines, identified at \u03bb\u00a0=\u00a011\u2009540\u2009\u00c5 and \u03bb\u00a0=\u00a011\u2009651\u2009\u00c5. These emission lines provide a robust spectroscopic redshift of z\u00a0=\u00a01.327 for the deflector galaxies.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig4.tiff\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/26154466/stv1872fig4.tiff\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig4.tiff\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"26154466\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/stv1872fig4.png?Expires=1611467343&Signature=jNufPlKqzMWa73ZJqv8ercMeGSvgrkevPC6ijIFH4jhPQO~pe~uEM3pM28wEacYJHJxGw49bnHbW5qLG2M9-JKwDMF5-vMzwRXHtWvRSadoVBYO4UrkS8uAMsioyn3d~d0TFBejPvbXdUA~x3e4cCqByB6GiHFTi7DAG5wYu4O-lTl80xRX5HYauAr9EKX~6pUNsgHCa4qBEkPDkKwnFXRm36wzQTb4kH02ylPOCKljUnVR7n-NAWGQdgc1thZO4WG6bWMlPHnSnpBgmGFkmeKhjzK1ZS68d-0XX~WkLgZZ7y5sxVeDqnNw1pIifp2UyCZFsCIy7uDG99G-bQ2etoA__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=26154466&ar=1752732&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig4.tiff\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The cropped two-dimensional spectrum of the central deflector galaxies, obtained using X-Shooter on the VLT. Top: the hydrogen\u00a0\u03b1 emission line, identified at \u03bb\u00a0=\u00a015\u2009272\u2009\u00c5. Bottom: The [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] doublet emission lines, identified at \u03bb\u00a0=\u00a011\u2009540\u2009\u00c5 and \u03bb\u00a0=\u00a011\u2009651\u2009\u00c5. These emission lines provide a robust spectroscopic redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327 for the deflector galaxies.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">It should be noted that there is a chance that the emission lines are coming only from the brighter foreground galaxy. However, the colours of the two central galaxies are virtually identical and we observe no emission lines at the location of the fainter galaxy elsewhere in the spectrum, leading to the likely possibility that the two galaxies are indeed a close pair at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327.</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=26154468 id=\"26154468\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-5-2>2.5.2 Constraints on the redshifts of the LBG</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Spectroscopic confirmation of high-redshift galaxies has been very difficult in the past, hence using gravitationally lensed LBGs provides the best opportunity to probe intrinsically fainter sources at high redshifts. The <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG candidate was included in our spectrum in order to search for the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emission line. The X-Shooter wavelength coverage would allow detection of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 line from a Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emitter at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a07, as well as other emission lines such is C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> (stark et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib62\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib62\" data-open=\"bib62\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015a</a>,<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib63\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib63\" data-open=\"bib63\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">b</a>). However we do not detect the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 line in the spectrum, nor do we detect any other emission lines. For an LBG residing at 7.6 \u2272 <em>z</em> \u2272 8.8 (the redshifts where there is a non-negligible probability density for this LBG), we show the 2D spectrum of the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> dropout at the wavelengths where Ly\u00a0\u03b1, C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> could conceivably appear is shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a>. We place upper limits on the equivalent widths of these lines in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2-5-3\"></span><a href=\"#sec2-5-3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2.5.3</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"26154470\" scrollto-destination=\"26154470\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig5.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=WjPq9x7fUClrGWHTqot8WJGkdNzN8IeNTuLcziKpay~5Z~XuhaNh9VsrNxVBustAzMdUNMLeWE4QrOQCXzowrmKy-TzCtuR3FI4mkN-A1IOhRV5dNAMErz7MOArxGfFKTFskO~THioAiHfekVvblDGSHDQKfYGYyqmqpd-n-qTMXu17bfsnEP~05pi24QqJ~r3x-GjqViP7GU06asTwGp4RhsY4WGfI2vtGxAxfqSw9V3SPV-OZlk7sLN6bK1akyKjJzlP3jKOQ6mdluPd89LlqMP2BuvA~Ecy7qcSzsV-8~h9V7hGDbWorQwwIpHs1cQ~m6T5bHvBbBwmUZuOG~lg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The regions of the 2D spectrum where the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 (1216\u2009\u00c5, top), C\u00a0iv (1548\u2009\u00c5, middle), and C\u00a0iii] (1909\u2009\u00c5, bottom) emission lines could appear given the redshift distribution of the dropout. The portion of the spectrum covering the dropout falls within the green lines. No lines are detected at these wavelengths or elsewhere in the spectrum at the location of the dropout. We use these non-detections to rule out a major class of low-redshift interlopers, and constrain the equivalent widths of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1, C\u00a0iii] and C\u00a0iv emission lines. The hydrogen\u00a0\u03b2 and [O\u00a0iii] doublet emission lines from the central galaxy pair are visible in the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 detection region at 11\u2009312, 11\u2009540 and 11\u2009651\u2009\u00c5, respectively.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig5.tiff\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/26154470/stv1872fig5.tiff\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig5.tiff\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"26154470\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/stv1872fig5.png?Expires=1611467343&Signature=Lw6qfGmwd7iBPP7BX4Ijh7AZ01G1WrZSIflNhfkueLP7XGAtxAil7W5KC9Tp7Gk6TbllBRVva17xxVHXzEWEe3ommqcNb2QYEvCl5iEfYRddXlQS-m0teDdWs428riSVhapTJ5h29MfsOw7v3R~zz8UjaTSdn7JQjkZQrMnUPgX49G6uxNugcFQdtaCyxH~kXdYWSaJsrE7r6jhjdksbHwWT-I3ShS3MqybosCKqZjuMN27bbRudf~Wy~TF4Uz2Ftv4fopkbmL6WRUlxEjGPujeUpclERhigwUlVeURJvVAoWdDDjt4r-vUuKPYAG02YhD6c7ianNX7bnzTkK5JYQA__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=26154470&ar=1752732&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig5.tiff\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The regions of the 2D spectrum where the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 (1216\u2009\u00c5, top), C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> (1548\u2009\u00c5, middle), and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] (1909\u2009\u00c5, bottom) emission lines could appear given the redshift distribution of the dropout. The portion of the spectrum covering the dropout falls within the green lines. No lines are detected at these wavelengths or elsewhere in the spectrum at the location of the dropout. We use these non-detections to rule out a major class of low-redshift interlopers, and constrain the equivalent widths of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1, C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> emission lines. The hydrogen\u00a0\u03b2 and [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] doublet emission lines from the central galaxy pair are visible in the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 detection region at 11\u2009312, 11\u2009540 and 11\u2009651\u2009\u00c5, respectively.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig5.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=WjPq9x7fUClrGWHTqot8WJGkdNzN8IeNTuLcziKpay~5Z~XuhaNh9VsrNxVBustAzMdUNMLeWE4QrOQCXzowrmKy-TzCtuR3FI4mkN-A1IOhRV5dNAMErz7MOArxGfFKTFskO~THioAiHfekVvblDGSHDQKfYGYyqmqpd-n-qTMXu17bfsnEP~05pi24QqJ~r3x-GjqViP7GU06asTwGp4RhsY4WGfI2vtGxAxfqSw9V3SPV-OZlk7sLN6bK1akyKjJzlP3jKOQ6mdluPd89LlqMP2BuvA~Ecy7qcSzsV-8~h9V7hGDbWorQwwIpHs1cQ~m6T5bHvBbBwmUZuOG~lg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The regions of the 2D spectrum where the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 (1216\u2009\u00c5, top), C\u00a0iv (1548\u2009\u00c5, middle), and C\u00a0iii] (1909\u2009\u00c5, bottom) emission lines could appear given the redshift distribution of the dropout. The portion of the spectrum covering the dropout falls within the green lines. No lines are detected at these wavelengths or elsewhere in the spectrum at the location of the dropout. We use these non-detections to rule out a major class of low-redshift interlopers, and constrain the equivalent widths of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1, C\u00a0iii] and C\u00a0iv emission lines. The hydrogen\u00a0\u03b2 and [O\u00a0iii] doublet emission lines from the central galaxy pair are visible in the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 detection region at 11\u2009312, 11\u2009540 and 11\u2009651\u2009\u00c5, respectively.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig5.tiff\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/26154470/stv1872fig5.tiff\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig5.tiff\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"26154470\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/stv1872fig5.png?Expires=1611467343&Signature=Lw6qfGmwd7iBPP7BX4Ijh7AZ01G1WrZSIflNhfkueLP7XGAtxAil7W5KC9Tp7Gk6TbllBRVva17xxVHXzEWEe3ommqcNb2QYEvCl5iEfYRddXlQS-m0teDdWs428riSVhapTJ5h29MfsOw7v3R~zz8UjaTSdn7JQjkZQrMnUPgX49G6uxNugcFQdtaCyxH~kXdYWSaJsrE7r6jhjdksbHwWT-I3ShS3MqybosCKqZjuMN27bbRudf~Wy~TF4Uz2Ftv4fopkbmL6WRUlxEjGPujeUpclERhigwUlVeURJvVAoWdDDjt4r-vUuKPYAG02YhD6c7ianNX7bnzTkK5JYQA__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=26154470&ar=1752732&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig5.tiff\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The regions of the 2D spectrum where the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 (1216\u2009\u00c5, top), C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> (1548\u2009\u00c5, middle), and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] (1909\u2009\u00c5, bottom) emission lines could appear given the redshift distribution of the dropout. The portion of the spectrum covering the dropout falls within the green lines. No lines are detected at these wavelengths or elsewhere in the spectrum at the location of the dropout. We use these non-detections to rule out a major class of low-redshift interlopers, and constrain the equivalent widths of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1, C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> emission lines. The hydrogen\u00a0\u03b2 and [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] doublet emission lines from the central galaxy pair are visible in the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 detection region at 11\u2009312, 11\u2009540 and 11\u2009651\u2009\u00c5, respectively.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Despite the lack of visible emission lines, the spectrum of the LBG candidate is nevertheless useful for constraining the strong lensing hypothesis since we can rule out the possibility of the source being a strong emission line contaminant. We do not observe any emission lines at the location of the dropout down to the sensitivity limit of our spectroscopic observations. While this prevents us from achieving spectroscopic confirmation, the non-detection of emission lines is important to exclude the most significant class of contaminants in samples of high-redshift LBGs. These contaminants are objects with a very weak continuum and very strong hydrogen\u00a0\u03b1, hydrogen\u00a0\u03b2 and [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] emission located at 1.3\u00a0\u2272\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0\u2272\u00a01.7, which could exhibit colours similar to those observed in the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 candidate of this paper (Atek et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We consider the noise levels of the dropout spectrum to place limits on the contribution to the observed broad-band flux from emission lines. The integrated line flux at \u03bb \u2248 1.6\u2009\u03bcm required to produce a broad-band flux of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{H_{160}}=25.75$|</span>\u00a0mag is 7.8\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221217</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup>. Assuming a simple model of an emission line with a width of 10\u2009\u00c5, the required flux density to account for all of the broad-band magnitude is 7.8\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221218</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup> \u2009\u00c5<sup>\u22121</sup>. The median noise in the spectrum in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> band is 4.6\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221219</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup> \u2009\u00c5<sup>\u22121</sup>. This allows us to rule out the presence of an emission line contributing more than <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{H_{160}}=28.6$|</span>\u00a0mag at 5\u03c3, and contributing all of the observed broad-band flux of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{H_{160}}=25.75$|</span>\u00a0mag at 70\u03c3. Similarly, the integrated line flux required to produce a broad-band flux of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{J_{125}}=25.92$|</span>\u00a0mag is 7.9\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221217</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup>, and the median noise level in the spectrum covering the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band is 1.0\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221218</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup> \u2009\u00c5<sup>\u22121</sup>. This allows us to rule out the presence of an emission line contributing more than <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{J_{125}}=27.9$|</span>\u00a0mag at 5\u03c3, and contributing the all of the observed broad-band flux of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{J_{125}}=25.92$|</span>\u00a0mag at 30\u03c3.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We calculate the likelihood that the emission lines are hidden behind sky lines or obscured by atmospheric absorption. We define the obscured part of the spectrum as the region where an emission line detected at 5\u03c3 at the median noise would be detected at less than 2\u03c3. The percentage of the spectrum covering the broad-band <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> filters obscured by sky lines or atmospheric absorption above the required level of emission lines is \u223c14\u00a0per\u00a0cent. If the dropout resides at 1.3\u00a0\u2272\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0\u2272\u00a01.7, the likelihood that both the brighter [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] emission line and hydrogen\u00a0\u03b1 line are obscured is 10\u00a0per\u00a0cent. The likelihood that the hydrogen\u00a0\u03b1 line and both of the [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] lines are obscured is 7\u00a0per\u00a0cent.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We conclude through this simple analysis that emission lines from the dropout source can contribute at most \u223c20\u00a0per\u00a0cent of the broad-band flux in <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and less than \u223c10\u00a0per\u00a0cent in <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>, therefore excluding lower redshift solutions with a faint (undetected) continuum and broad-band photometry dominated by strong emission lines with very high confidence.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">As a consistency check, we compare the required luminosity of the emission lines in the case of the dropout being a low-redshift interloper with the detected emission lines of the foreground galaxies. For emission lines to contribute the required flux in <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> for the dropout, they would need to be as bright as the observed [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] 4959\u2009\u00c5 line from the foreground galaxy pair, and twice as bright as the observed hydrogen\u00a0\u03b2 line, both of which are detected with high confidence (\u227310\u03c3).</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=26154476 id=\"26154476\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-5-3>2.5.3 Equivalent width constraints from the LBG spectrum</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In addition to ruling out strong emission line interlopers, the absence of emission lines allows us to place upper limits on the equivalent widths of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1, C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> emission lines for this LBG. Each of these emission lines have been observed in spectra of LBGs at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a06 previously (Ono et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib52\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib52\" data-open=\"bib52\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Finkelstein et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Oesch et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib50\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib50\" data-open=\"bib50\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Stark et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib62\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib62\" data-open=\"bib62\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015a</a>,<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib63\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib63\" data-open=\"bib63\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">b</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We investigate the limits that can be placed on the equivalent width of Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emission. We do this by assuming a half-Gaussian model of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emission line profile with a full width at half-maximum (FWHM) of 12\u2009\u00c5. We calculate the 5\u03c3 upper limit on the integrated line flux by considering the noise in the spectrum in the possible wavelength range of Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emission. The continuum flux density is computed from the broad-band photometry. The result is a median 5\u03c3 upper limit of the rest-frame equivalent width of EW<sub>0</sub>(Ly\u00a0\u03b1)\u00a0&lt;\u00a057\u2009\u00c5. We quantify the chance that Ly\u00a0\u03b1 is obscured by sky lines or atmospheric absorption in the region where we expect Ly\u00a0\u03b1 to appear. The redshift distribution for the LBG is centred on <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a08, but there is a non-negligible probability density from <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a07.6 to 8.8. Using the range of wavelengths at which Ly\u00a0\u03b1 could appear, we calculate that the chance that it has been obscured to be 14\u00a0per\u00a0cent.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We also constrain the equivalent width of C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> emission lines. For these emission lines, we assume a Gaussian emission line profile model with an FWHM of 12\u2009\u00c5. We calculate the 5\u03c3 upper limit on the integrated line flux by considering the noise in the spectrum in the possible wavelength range of C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> emission. The continuum flux density is again calculated from the broad-band photometry. The results are median 5\u03c3 upper limits for C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> emission of EW<sub>0</sub>(C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>])\u00a0&lt;\u00a025\u2009\u00c5 and EW<sub>0</sub>(C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>)\u00a0&lt;\u00a036\u2009\u00c5, respectively. We quantify the chance of the C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> lines being obscured by sky lines or due to atmospheric absorption as 12\u00a0per\u00a0cent in both cases.</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=26154480 id=\"26154480\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-5-4>2.5.4 Photometric redshift of the third foreground galaxy</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The X-Shooter slit does not cover the third nearby foreground galaxy (ID: 650). To constrain the redshift of this source, we utilize the Bayesian photometric redshift code <span class=\"small-caps\">bpz</span> (Benitez <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>; Ben\u00edtez et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Coe et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>). The photometric redshift distribution of this source is characterized by a more extended probability distribution, peaking at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a00.3. However, there is a non-negligible peak in the likelihood distribution centred at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.3, leading to the distinct possibility that this galaxy is at the same redshift as the central objects and the broad redshift distribution is simply an effect of photometric scatter. The photometric redshift distribution for this third galaxy is shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"26154482\" scrollto-destination=\"26154482\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig6\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 6.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig6.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=GW3khDfS3Dfq4omz5JUWiIZBZFz1im3MBVXo~pO4pzmH1mqlleSSqWxpCV8mA-sxRjeKJdzfJSM1kneJCXiSfKZ6IHS4mXpq1-x4AogFPoybkpRRtVx8GObx1iGITfSHpmp15a1kgxEVJtlwCaigNc5V-Z8dBRsWqn~PWfwM4A3H1gDRhrQv3Qtp1Xd5~-EAFiXHzDbAlNPg26qiwWfsFF5BFtz9KW~Zkz9PKA-rE8eDdXGLZlu5Mb9Z8bhbETiGli9HF596qAVVQOM59RMIT-32~fw2yYy~Vh-UO7G5bxciQEqS5V8EDDeK6-reUGOBT7k-F1mkyRtmDvmTPr2m2Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The redshift probability distribution function for the third foreground galaxy (ID: 650), obtained with the photometric redshift code bpz using the Hubble Ultra Deep Field prior.
