(<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). The red dotted lines mark the observed separation between borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_682$|</span> and borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_647$|</span> (1.8\u00a0arcsec). The likelihood of this random alignment is \u223c1.7\u00a0per\u00a0cent, and the likelihood of strong lensing is \u223c23\u00a0per\u00a0cent.</p></div></div><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Bayes Theorem gives a similar result, where the likelihood of strong lensing (\u2018SL\u2019) given the observed separation between a high-redshift object and a foreground object can be expressed as <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ4\" content-id=\"equ4\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\nP(\\rm {SL}\\theta \\le 1.8\\,{\\rm arcsec\\,})=\\frac{P(\\theta \\le 1.8\\,{\\rm arcsec\\,}\\rm {SL})}{P(\\theta \\le 1.8\\,{\\rm arcsec})}P(\\rm {SL}),\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(4)</span></div>where we can estimate values for <em>P</em>(SL) and <em>P</em>(\u03b8\u00a0\u2264\u00a01.8\u2009arcsec\u2009SL) from fig. 4 of Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) and <em>P</em>(\u03b8\u00a0\u2264\u00a01.8\u2009arcsec) from Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig11\" data-open=\"fig11\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">11</a>, and find that, <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ5\" content-id=\"equ5\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray}\r\nP(\\rm {SL}\\theta \\le 1.8\\,{\\rm arcsec})\\;\\simeq \\;\\frac{0.6}{0.017}\\times 0.008\r\n\\end{eqnarray} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(5)</span></div><div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ6\" content-id=\"equ6\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray}\r\n\\hphantom{P(\\rm {SL}\\theta \\le 1.8\\,{\\rm arcsec})\\;}=28 \\,\\mathrm{per\\ cent}.\r\n\\end{eqnarray} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(6)</span></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154524 id=\"26154524\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6-3>6.3 The foreground objects are typical deflectors of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBGs</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In the study of gravitational lensing in the CANDELS fields by Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), they presented the distribution of deflector luminosities, redshifts and deflector-source separation (see fig. 4 of Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). The spectroscopic redshift of the central foreground galaxy pair is consistent with the observed peak of the redshift distribution for gravitational lenses of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a07\u20138 LBGs, which occurs between <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a01 and 2. The observed separation between the central foreground objects and the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG candidate, \u03b8<sub>sep</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.8\u00a0arcsec, is also at the peak of the deflector-source separation distribution, which peaks at 1.5\u00a0&lt;\u00a0\u03b8<sub>sep</sub>\u00a0&lt;\u00a02.0\u00a0arcsec. The luminosity of the central object is also near the peak of the absolute magnitude distribution. Additionally, the required Einstein radius derived in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a> of \u223c1.5\u00a0arcsec is consistent with strong lensing by a massive galaxy/group at moderate redshift (Treu &amp; Koopmans <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib71\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib71\" data-open=\"bib71\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Treu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib70\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib70\" data-open=\"bib70\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Newman, Ellis &amp; Treu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Further to the point of the objects borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_647$|</span> and borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_650$|</span> being in the range of luminosities of gravitational deflectors in the CANDELS fields identified by Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), we can also infer the mass of these galaxies using abundance matching. Based on modelling of the galaxy luminosity function at high redshift (Trenti, Perna &amp; Jimenez <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib69\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib69\" data-open=\"bib69\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), abundance matching of the luminosity of the object borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_647$|</span> translates to an halo mass of \u223c5.7\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>12</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>. The object borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_650$|</span>'s luminosity translates to a halo mass of \u223c1.0\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>12</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub> if it is also at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a01.3.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Associating these masses with the virial mass, and circular velocities with the virial velocity, this mass would give circular velocities <em>V</em><sub>c</sub>\u00a0\u223c\u00a0270 and 150 kms<sup>\u22121</sup> for the haloes of the two galaxies borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_647$|</span> and borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_650$|\u2060</span>, respectively. Translating circular velocities into central stellar velocity dispersions \u03c3<sub>\u22c6</sub> of an isothermal model for the deflector is complicated by baryonic physics which generally tend to increase the central velocity dispersion of a collapsed Navarro, Frenk &amp; White (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib45\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib45\" data-open=\"bib45\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1997</a>) DM halo. In practice, the circular velocity is comparable to the observed stellar velocity dispersion \u03c3<sub>\u22c6</sub>\u00a0\u2248\u00a0<em>V</em><sub>c</sub> at the scale considered here (e.g. Bundy, Treu &amp; Ellis <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Dutton et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>), which is in turn very close to the velocity dispersion of the singular isothermal sphere that describes the total mass density profile in the inner regions of massive ellipticals (Treu &amp; Koopmans <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib72\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib72\" data-open=\"bib72\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Koopmans et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>; Auger et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010b</a>). In addition, the gravitational lensing optical depth is a strongly rising function of velocity dispersion (e.g. Ruff et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib56\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib56\" data-open=\"bib56\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>) and \u03c3<sub>\u22c6</sub>\u00a0\u2248\u00a0300\u2009kms<sup>\u22121</sup> is a typical value for group-sized haloes (Treu &amp; Koopmans <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib71\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib71\" data-open=\"bib71\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>). These inferred velocity dispersions are sufficient to produce an Einstein radius of the magnitude required in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a>.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154528 id=\"26154528\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6-4>6.4 Possible multiple imaging</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Multiple imaging by a deflector is a necessary condition for strong lensing, although secondary images of the source will appear much fainter and closer to the deflector galaxy, making them difficult to detect at high significance (Wyithe et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib82\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib82\" data-open=\"bib82\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Fialkov &amp; Loeb <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). Consistent with this, we observe a possible faint counter image on the opposite side of the central deflector objects. Both the brighter image and the fainter image are completely absent in the <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> and <em>V</em><sub>600</sub> filters, consistent with the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG selection criteria, and with the lensing hypothesis, as gravitational lensing is achromatic. The colours of the counter image are consistent with both the <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>-dropout, and being a <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 object below the flux limit of the BoRG field. The observed flux ratio between the two images is consistent with the flux ratio predicted in the best-fitting model in our lens modelling.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">As discussed in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2-4\"></span><a href=\"#sec2-4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2.4</a>, the counter image is not detected in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> image. This is expected based on the colours of the source and the sensitivity of the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> and <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> images.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154531 id=\"26154531\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6-5>6.5 Elongation of the dropout</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG is consistent with being elongated tangentially to the direction to the central foreground galaxies. In gravitational lensing theory, images are elongated into arcs and arclets along the critical curves of deflectors. Unless the deflector has very high ellipticity, the image's elongation will always be tangential to the direction from the image to the deflector. As described in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2-3\"></span><a href=\"#sec2-3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2.3</a>, the primary image shows elongation that is tangential to the direction towards the central foreground galaxies with ellipticity of \u03f5\u00a0=\u00a00.4\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1. Our modelling of the system confirms that the observed elongation is consistent with that predicted by the model once smearing by the WFC3 PSF and low S/N of the data are taken into account.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154533 id=\"26154533\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6-6>6.6 Lack of companion dropouts in the field</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Finally, we note that the field contains only this single candidate detected at high S/N. Based on DM clustering, we expect additional dropouts in the field if the primary image is not strongly magnified. Abundance matching predicts that the dropout is hosted in a rare DM halo with <em>M</em><sub>DM</sub> \u2273 2 \u00d7 10<sup>11</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub> (Mu\u00f1oz &amp; Loeb <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib44\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib44\" data-open=\"bib44\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Trenti et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib68\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib68\" data-open=\"bib68\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). However, the connection between DM halo mass and galaxy luminosity seems unclear at high redshift, as highlighted by the recent measurement of the two-point correlation function at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a07 from CANDELS and XDF catalogues (Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) and by the lack of strong clustering around a more luminous and isolated galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a07.7 (Oesch et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib50\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib50\" data-open=\"bib50\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). Therefore, while the lensing hypothesis provides a natural explanation of this single bright candidate (the dropout would be intrinsically fainter and hence less clustered), further studies are needed to use the lack of clustering as a quantitative support for the lensing hypothesis.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154535 id=\"26154535\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6-7>6.7 Comparison with previous lensing studies of the BoRG sample</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The configuration we have investigated in this paper was not identified in the analysis of Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) as a strong lensing candidate. Based on a Faber\u2013Jackson relation (Faber &amp; Jackson <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1976</a>), Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) only identified a single different object from our high-S/N sample as a candidate for being gravitationally magnified by a foreground object (inferring a magnification for that object of \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a01.47\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.3). However, there are a number of reasons that the galaxy we have identified in this paper was missed by Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). First, we have obtained additional spectroscopy which places the nearby objects at a lower redshift than the photometric redshift used in the Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) analysis, which leads to a lower required mass for strong gravitational lensing. Secondly, the Faber\u2013Jackson relation used by Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) will underestimate the lensing potential of a gravitational deflector which consists of multiple objects, because gravitational magnification is not linearly additive (Wong et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib79\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib79\" data-open=\"bib79\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) and much more DM is expected in group environments.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We find that when the central foreground galaxy pair, which is identified as a single object in the BoRG catalogue, is considered at its correct redshift, the estimated magnification of borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_682$|</span> in the Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) framework increases by \u223c10\u00a0per\u00a0cent to \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a01.41. We also infer the magnification using velocity dispersions found using the Faber\u2013Jackson relation of Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) and their lensing likelihood framework, which leads to the estimated magnification of borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_682$|</span> to be <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mu =1.47^{+0.30}_{-0.18}$|\u2060</span>, and a strong lensing likelihood of 11\u00a0per\u00a0cent. There are only seven objects in the Bouwens et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) sample of 155 <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG candidates that Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) deemed to have a likelihood of lensing than higher than 11\u00a0per\u00a0cent.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">If the object borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_650$|</span> also resides at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.3 and is included as a third deflector, the magnification further increases at the location of the dropout. In fact, when including this third lensing galaxy at <em>z</em> \u2243 1.3 and using the velocity dispersions inferred from the FJR of Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), the magnification at the location of the dropout is <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mu =1.96^{+0.63}_{-0.36}$|\u2060</span>, giving it a strong lensing likelihood of 47\u00a0per\u00a0cent.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The case presented in this paper highlights that the available photometry of both the source LBG and the photometric and spectroscopic observations of the foreground group, and the inferences on the group's mass, are completely consistent with this configuration resulting in a high magnification in the LBG. In fact, the foreground group would need a peculiarly low mass given its luminosity for there to be low magnification (\u03bc\u00a0\u2272\u00a01.4) of the source LBG.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=26154540 id=\"26154540\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec7>7 CONCLUSION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In this paper, we use broad-band <em>HST</em> photometry to identify a candidate galaxy-scale gravitational lensing system composed of a <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG source and a small foreground group. To follow-up the system, we have obtained very deep VLT/X-Shooter spectroscopy of the LBG and two members of the group. Our new spectroscopic data confirm that the foreground galaxy pair has a redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327 through detection of multiple emission lines. A third possible foreground deflector galaxy, not targeted by spectroscopy, has an extended photometric redshift distribution, with a non-negligible likelihood around <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.3. The X-Shooter spectroscopy also allows us to exclude the LBG candidate as a low-redshift interloper with strong emission lines with high confidence (70\u2009\u03c3 in <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>). Therefore, due to the small angular separation between the LBG and the foreground galaxies, the foreground galaxy pair's spectroscopic redshift and the ruling out of lower redshift solutions for the LBG from the absence of emission lines, the dropout must have been gravitationally magnified to some degree. In this paper, we carried out a detailed modelling with the goal of quantifying the magnification. We argue that the most likely configuration is that the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 source has been magnified by \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a04.3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2, producing a secondary demagnified image on the opposite side of the deflector galaxies. We marginally detect this secondary image (with S/N\u00a0\u223c\u00a02) in the band with the deepest imaging, <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The lens model yields a total group mass of 9.62\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.31\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>11</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>, which is very close to the mass expected from abundance matching. We have obtained a lensing measurement of the stellar mass of a compact galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327, without being affected by the systematic uncertainties that are associated with the inference of stellar mass from spectral energy distribution using population synthesis models. Assuming the standard DM fraction found for lower redshift lenses, the brighter central deflector galaxy has a stellar mass-to-light ratio of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$M_{\\star }/L_{B} = 2.3^{+0.8}_{-0.6} \\,\\mathrm{M}_{{\\odot }}/\\mathrm{L}_{{\\odot }}$|</span> within its effective radius. Overall, the properties of the main lensing galaxy are consistent with observations of \u2018red nuggets\u2019 at similar redshifts (Daddi et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2005</a>; Trujillo et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib75\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib75\" data-open=\"bib75\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Buitrago et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Van Dokkum et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib76\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib76\" data-open=\"bib76\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>). This represents a leap forward compared to other similar measurements from gravitational lensing, which are limited to <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2272\u00a01 (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig10\" data-open=\"fig10\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">10</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Using this interpretation of the data, we find a strongly lensed fraction of galaxies bright than \u2248<em>M</em><sub>\u22c6</sub> in BoRG to be 10\u00a0per\u00a0cent. While the uncertainty on this number is large due to the rarity of bright <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 objects, this value is quantitatively consistent with the findings of Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), who found an expected strongly lensed fraction of 3\u201315\u00a0per\u00a0cent in the BoRG fields, the recent analysis of the CANDELS fields and the XDF by Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) and theoretical modelling by Wyithe et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib82\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib82\" data-open=\"bib82\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). Since Wyithe et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib82\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib82\" data-open=\"bib82\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>) showed that the effect of magnification bias on the galaxy luminosity function increases with redshift, quantifying and verifying its impact at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 is important for predictions for future surveys targeted at finding <em>L</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a0<em>L</em><sub>\u22c6</sub> galaxies at yet higher redshift, such as <em>Euclid</em> and surveys using <em>JWST</em> and <em>WFIRST</em>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Overall, the strong lensing configuration derived by our work is the most natural interpretation, but a more precise measurement of the magnification of the source and the counter image would allow more robust inferences about the system. Intriguingly, our modelling makes specific predictions testable with deeper <em>HST</em> imaging, including the precise flux ratio between the two images and the elongation of the brighter image. Improving the S/N of the observations by a factor of 2 would allow both these measurements and hence allow a better determination of the magnification of this <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG. Such a goal is within reach of <em>HST</em> as it would require only \u223c10 orbits of observations.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This work is partially supported by programmes number HST/GO 11700, 12587, 12905 and 13767 from NASA through a grant from the Space Telescope Science Institute, which is operated by the Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy, Inc, under NASA contract NAS5-26555. JSBW acknowledges the support of an Australian Research Council Laureate Fellowship. MT acknowledges the support of an Australia Research Council Future Fellowship. We would like to acknowledge the anonymous referee for their helpful comments, Sharon Rapoport for her initial lens modelling of the system and Stephanie Bernard for her help with the BoRG data.</p><div content-id=\"fn1\"><span class=\"fn\"><span class=\"label fn-label\"><span rel=\"nofollow\" data-fn-id=\"fn1\" class=\"end-note-link\">1</span></span><div class=\"footnote-content\"><p class=\"footnote-compatibility\">This analysis is based on observations of the CANDELS fields using the methodology of Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p></div></span></div> type=\"hidden\" value=\"mnras\" /> \n    </div>\n\r\n                    </div>\r\n                </div>\r\n            </div>\r\n            <div id=\"ContentTab\" class=\"content active\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=26154430 id=\"26154430\" class=\"abstract-title\" >Abstract</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We present a detailed analysis of an individual case of gravitational lensing of a <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 Lyman-break galaxy (LBG) in a blank field, identified in <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> imaging obtained as part of the Brightest of Reionizing Galaxies survey. To investigate the close proximity of the bright (<em>m</em><sub><em>AB</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a025.8) <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>-dropout to a small group of foreground galaxies, we obtained deep spectroscopy of the dropout and two foreground galaxies using VLT/X-Shooter. We detect H\u00a0\u03b1, H\u00a0\u03b2, [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] emission in the brightest two foreground galaxies (unresolved at the natural seeing of 0.8\u00a0arcsec), placing the pair at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327. We can rule out emission lines contributing all of the observed broad-band flux in <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> band at 70\u03c3, allowing us to exclude the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 candidate as a low-redshift interloper with broad-band photometry dominated by strong emission lines. The foreground galaxy pair lies at the peak of the luminosity, redshift and separation distributions for deflectors of strongly lensed <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 objects, and we make a marginal detection of a demagnified secondary image in the deepest (<em>J</em><sub>125</sub>) filter. We show that the configuration can be accurately modelled by a singular isothermal ellipsoidal deflector and a S\u00e9rsic source magnified by a factor of \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a04.3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2. The reconstructed source in the best-fitting model is consistent with luminosities and morphologies of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBGs in the literature. The lens model yields a group mass of 9.62\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.31\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>11</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub> and a stellar mass-to-light ratio for the brightest deflector galaxy of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$M_{\\star }/L_{B}=2.3^{+0.8}_{-0.6} \\,\\mathrm{M}_{{\\odot }}/\\mathrm{L}_{{\\odot }}$|</span> within its effective radius. The foreground galaxies\u2019 redshifts would make this one of the few strong lensing deflectors discovered at <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a01. Deeper imaging would allow for confirmation of the existence of the secondary image and elongation in the primary image, verifying multiple imaging and producing more robust estimations of the image magnifications.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: high-redshift&quot;\">galaxies: high-redshift</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;cosmology: observations&quot;\">cosmology: observations</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=26154432 id=\"26154432\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The epoch of reionization at redshift <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a07\u201312 (Komatsu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib39\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib39\" data-open=\"bib39\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Shull et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib61\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib61\" data-open=\"bib61\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Planck Collaboration I <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib53\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib53\" data-open=\"bib53\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>) is a key period in the evolution of the Universe when the first galaxies formed and reionized the neutral hydrogen in the intergalactic medium. Due to the absorption of emitted photons with energies high enough to ionize neutral hydrogen, the spectra of these early galaxies have highly attenuated regions bluer than the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 break at 1216\u2009\u00c5, enabling their identification from broad-band imaging with the Lyman-break, or \u2018dropout\u2019, technique (Steidel et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib64\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib64\" data-open=\"bib64\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>; Giavalisco <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>). This technique has been used successfully to build large galaxy samples out to <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08, with sources selected using observations from both ground- and space-based observatories (e.g. Bradley et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; McLure et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib41\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib41\" data-open=\"bib41\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Finkelstein et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Schmidt et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib58\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib58\" data-open=\"bib58\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Bouwens et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">These new observations have opened the possibility of quantifying and studying the galaxy luminosity function during the epoch of reionization as well as its evolution with redshift (Khochfar et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Bouwens et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Castellano et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Trenti et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib66\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib66\" data-open=\"bib66\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Bradley et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Finkelstein et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Oesch et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib49\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib49\" data-open=\"bib49\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; McLure et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib41\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib41\" data-open=\"bib41\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Robertson et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib54\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib54\" data-open=\"bib54\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib55\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib55\" data-open=\"bib55\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Schenker et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib57\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib57\" data-open=\"bib57\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Finkelstein et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Schmidt et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib58\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib58\" data-open=\"bib58\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Measurement of the luminosity function is a key requirement for understanding the production of ionizing photons at high redshift, which completes hydrogen reionization. In this context, it is of fundamental importance to discriminate between intrinsic evolution of the galaxy luminosity function and observational selection effects.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">One possible effect is gravitational lensing magnification bias (e.g. Wallington &amp; Narayan <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib77\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib77\" data-open=\"bib77\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1993</a>). While the fraction of random lines of sight at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a06 that are strongly gravitationally lensed by massive foreground galaxies is around \u223c0.5\u00a0per\u00a0cent (Barkana &amp; Loeb <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>; Comerford, Haiman &amp; Schaye <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Wyithe et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib82\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib82\" data-open=\"bib82\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Mason et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), the steep nature of the high-redshift luminosity function results in observationally bright Lyman-break galaxies (LBGs) having an excess likelihood of having been gravitationally lensed (Wyithe et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib82\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib82\" data-open=\"bib82\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Fialkov &amp; Loeb <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). In general, magnification bias depends on the slope of the luminosity function of the source galaxies: steeper luminosity functions yield more lensed sources because the loss in solid angle is compensated by the steep rise in number counts at deeper flux limits. Therefore, this effect becomes especially important for the bright end of the galaxy luminosity function (<em>L</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a0<em>L</em><sub>\u22c6</sub>), where <em>L</em><sub>\u22c6</sub> is the \u2018knee\u2019 of the luminosity function in the Schechter parametrization, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\phi (L){\\rm d}L = \\phi _{\\star }(L/L_{\\star })^{\\alpha } \\exp ^{-(L/L_{\\star })}{\\rm d}(L/L_{\\star })$|\u2060</span>. In Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), we showed that magnification bias exists in LBG surveys at\u00a0\u22734, and becomes a significant factor in surveys of LBGs at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a07, with \u223c10\u00a0per\u00a0cent of LBGs brighter than <em>L</em><sub>\u22c6</sub> strongly lensed in fields without massive structures such as the Hubble eXtreme Deep Field (XDF; Illingworth et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>), and Cosmic Assembly Near-infrared Deep Extragalactic Legacy Survey fields (CANDELS; Grogin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib32\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib32\" data-open=\"bib32\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Koekemoer et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib38\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib38\" data-open=\"bib38\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The results in Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) confirm the prediction of Wyithe et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib82\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib82\" data-open=\"bib82\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>) that \u223c10\u00a0per\u00a0cent of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBGs in a survey with a flux limit around <em>M</em><sub>\u22c6</sub>, such as the Brightest of Reionizing Galaxies (BoRG) WFC3 <em>HST</em> survey (Trenti et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib68\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib68\" data-open=\"bib68\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Bradley et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), could be strongly lensed. Hence the BoRG survey offers the perfect data set to extend the findings of Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). In fact, an analysis of the BoRG survey by Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) found that 3\u201315\u00a0per\u00a0cent of LBGs in the BoRG fields are expected to be strongly lensed, depending on the specific flux limit of each field. They also investigated individual <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 candidates in the BoRG survey and found one good candidate for strong gravitational lensing, having an estimated magnification of \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a02.02\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.52. They also identified a further three candidates with lower magnifications of \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a01.80\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.33, 1.54\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.62 and 1.47\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.30.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The relatively small number of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 candidates in the BoRG survey do not allow a statistical approach, such as that undertaken by Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), to detect evidence of gravitational lensing. In this paper, we adopt a direct approach to search for evidence of gravitational lensing by looking at individual LBGs. We only consider the highest signal-to-noise (S/N) LBGs in the BoRG sample, which includes 10 candidates detected at S/N\u00a0\u2265\u00a08\u03c3 and <em>m</em>\u00a0\u2272\u00a027 (\u2248<em>M</em><sub>\u22c6</sub> at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08). The results from Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) and Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) imply that \u22481 of these LBGs should be strongly gravitationally lensed. We inspected these 10 LBGs searching for potential gravitationally lensed configurations, and find one <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 candidate in close projection to a foreground group of galaxies.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This paper is structured as follows. We discuss the data, photometry and spectroscopy in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a>, we introduce the Markov-Chain Monte Carlo (MCMC) method that we have applied to investigate the lensing hypothesis, as well as the MCMC results. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>, we compare the inferred <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 source properties to those in the literature. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>, we investigate the properties of the deflector. We discuss the evidence for lensing in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec6\"></span><a href=\"#sec6\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">6</a>, and we conclude in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec7\"></span><a href=\"#sec7\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">7</a>. Throughout this paper we assume a \u039bCDM cosmology of \u03a9<sub>M</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.27, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.73 and <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a070kms<sup>\u22121</sup>Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>. We quote magnitudes in the AB system (Oke &amp; Gunn <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib51\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib51\" data-open=\"bib51\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1983</a>). We refer to the <em>F</em>600<em>LP</em>, <em>F</em>098<em>M</em>, <em>F</em>125<em>W</em> and <em>F</em>160<em>W</em><em>HST</em> filters as <em>V</em><sub>600</sub>, <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>, <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=26154439 id=\"26154439\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 THE SEARCH FOR STRONG GRAVITATIONAL LENSING IN THE BRIGHTEST OF REIONIZING GALAXIES SURVEY</h2>\r\n                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154440 id=\"26154440\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-1>2.1 The BoRG survey</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The BoRG survey is a Hubble Wide-Field Camera 3 (WFC3) large, multiyear pure-parallel programme aimed at identifying galaxy candidates at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a07.5 from their colours based on the Lyman-break technique (Steidel et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib64\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib64\" data-open=\"bib64\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1996</a>). Until recently, the main focus of BoRG has been identification of galaxies at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 as <em>Y</em>-band dropouts, while ongoing observations (cycle 22; #13767; PI Trenti) are optimized for selecting <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08\u20139 candidates.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In this work, we use data from observations acquired before cycle 22. The core of this earlier data set is based on WFC3 imaging in four filters (<em>V</em><sub>606</sub>, <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>, <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>, <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>) obtained as part of <em>HST</em> programmes #11700 and #12572 (PI Trenti), complemented by archival data with a similar observational design and the same infrared filters, but with <em>F</em>600<em>LP</em> substituting <em>F</em>606<em>W</em> (<em>HST</em> program #11702, PI Yan; Yan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib83\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib83\" data-open=\"bib83\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). A full description of the survey and of its findings is reported by Trenti et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib67\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib67\" data-open=\"bib67\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib68\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib68\" data-open=\"bib68\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), Bradley et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) and Schmidt et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib58\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib58\" data-open=\"bib58\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). To summarize, the last comprehensive data release of the BoRG survey yielded <em>n</em>\u00a0=\u00a038 <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG candidates identified as <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>-dropouts with <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> magnitudes between 25.5 and 27.6\u00a0mag (Schmidt et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib58\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib58\" data-open=\"bib58\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). These candidates were obtained by analysing data over a total area of 350\u00a0arcmin<sup>2</sup> divided in 71 independent lines of sight.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154443 id=\"26154443\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-2>2.2 Search for a candidate strongly lensed <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The large number of independent fields in BoRG results in a sample essentially unaffected by large-scale structure uncertainty (Trenti &amp; Stiavelli <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>), and includes a variety of different environments in terms of line-of-sight structure, representing an ideal data set to quantify magnification bias in a different manner to that used by Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) and Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). To search for evidence of large magnifications, we have visually inspected the regions surrounding the 10 sources detected with an S/N\u00a0\u2265\u00a08\u03c3 in the BoRG survey, all of which have <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{J_{125}}\\leq 27.0$|</span> searching for evidence of strong gravitational lensing. We investigate only the highest S/N objects because they offer the best chance of identifying direct evidence of strong lensing in the event that they have been significantly magnified. Indications of strong gravitational lensing that we inspect for are proximity of the dropout to bright foreground objects, and secondary images with similar colours to the dropout. Cutouts of the 10 candidates in the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band are shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"26154445\" scrollto-destination=\"26154445\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig1.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=uPvrR2OaB5cDyIThE~GtljZZ-vunCVv25BwaDKjJdnxUEL17aI8kq45bI6IJ4ZIqeTC7UwfnoGTz4H~MwnnOhBn0vSON2gKUgk6MG18xJZfnZUzgQd7PLwU-zI1uUvCMmq6Hu1ZMvUgXp9WRgFvD0H~MVbWA4EcL6bW5Psreud69XFLbRZ~p52AEw0g5FWkA2jRMSAdZFWhzjrN6uKv3125GEA7c3UzI37WIgbvvAIcNcN9SpJYpxf~a52J54yebtvh6bA9BjSpGBTlxyvP4mhOrfT~7BIp2UFBL0mFqeME~nrTah9yRGHZxAaolQLYFgiRD4BOIYV~MwDzQgxOSKQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The 10 8\u03c3 z\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG candidates identified in the BoRG survey. The cutouts are 5\u00a0arcsec on each side, which is the characteristic scale for galaxy\u2013galaxy lensing (Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. 2015), and shown in the J125 band. Seven of the 10 candidates are ruled out as being strongly gravitationally lensed due to the absence of foreground objects along the line of sight. The object borg$\\_1301$+$0000\\_160$ appears nearby a bright foreground galaxy, and Mason et\u00a0al. (2015) assess its magnification to be \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a01.47\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.30. The object borg$\\_1437$+$5043\\_1137$ appears 2.6\u00a0arcsec from a bright foreground at zphot\u00a0=\u00a01.4. Using the framework of Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (2015), this object has a magnification of \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a01.3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2 and a 5\u00a0per\u00a0cent chance of being strongly lensed. Neither of these configurations display obvious secondary images, which is the key criterion for constraining strong lensing. The object borg$\\_0440$-$5244\\_682$ is in close proximity to a group of three foreground galaxies, around which a candidate secondary image is identified.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig1.tiff\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/26154445/stv1872fig1.tiff\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig1.tiff\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"26154445\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/stv1872fig1.png?Expires=1611467343&Signature=4C-I308tHibToYfpvgsRk2SAgwJkEiqvGywQeiS2jXNmu6bA9KZTht~~qepK7NMhb91~hZCNfNWsmo2GY5xR1T9JZtXTipxwOZiROxoSgsCLl9r5zw6sLliwH--uXMOHdMPqSbJnTjXW4Pyw4ltf4VUzkNJR--uul48BvKWQrNFlh1oTm-B1D4s7vSpgVdtCB~3w9PAQ4nYFmHiCS5BSUb-bjtKhejeOEFqnmqQfYVpINqPk65YyM6Ctg2CWFqJL6A-c39~IVlkRgth-FkaQ7tPGzTHsgjIaKIkTS2Ft~6H7~i9tgkOT-Ubhwx00IQrXqcot-NvB7ukQxSiU-ZRkcQ__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=26154445&ar=1752732&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig1.tiff\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The 10 8\u03c3 <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG candidates identified in the BoRG survey. The cutouts are 5\u00a0arcsec on each side, which is the characteristic scale for galaxy\u2013galaxy lensing (Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), and shown in the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band. Seven of the 10 candidates are ruled out as being strongly gravitationally lensed due to the absence of foreground objects along the line of sight. The object borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_1301$|</span>+<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$0000\\_160$|</span> appears nearby a bright foreground galaxy, and Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) assess its magnification to be \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a01.47\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.30. The object borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_1437$|</span>+<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5043\\_1137$|</span> appears 2.6\u00a0arcsec from a bright foreground at <em>z</em><sub>phot</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.4. Using the framework of Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), this object has a magnification of \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a01.3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2 and a 5\u00a0per\u00a0cent chance of being strongly lensed. Neither of these configurations display obvious secondary images, which is the key criterion for constraining strong lensing. The object borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_682$|</span> is in close proximity to a group of three foreground galaxies, around which a candidate secondary image is identified.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">We identify one good candidate for a strongly gravitationally lensed <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG (borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_682$|</span> in the notation of Bradley et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), which appears very close in projection to a compact grouping of three foreground galaxies (borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_647$|\u2060</span>, which consists of two objects, and borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_650$|\u2060</span>). Through visual inspection of the configuration, we identify a possible faint (S/N\u00a0\u223c\u00a02) counter image, which appears in the deepest band, <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>, and is located immediately below the foreground galaxies opposite the location of the dropout. The location and flux relative to the brighter image is consistent with gravitational lensing theory, which predicts secondary images to appear demagnified on the opposite side of the deflector, and at a smaller separation from the deflector than the brighter image. In fact, a strikingly similar gravitational lensing configuration has been observed (Wong et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib80\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib80\" data-open=\"bib80\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>, see fig. 3) with almost identical relative image positions, magnifications and flux ratio, albeit with a lower redshift source and smaller deflection angles.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The proximity to multiple bright foreground galaxies and identification of a possible secondary image with similar colours to the dropout makes <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\rm borg}\\_0440\\_5244\\_682$|</span> a good candidate to be significantly magnified, warranting further investigation. Postage-stamp images of the dropout and foreground galaxies in the single optical and three near-IR filters of the BoRG survey are presented in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>, where the objects are labelled in the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> panel.</p>                        <a id=\"26154448\" scrollto-destination=\"26154448\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig2.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=WYOng0IG21t894YfyqbcN40Ih06nj0X573y8us-vi2Ol~bj16Dkmc8GMb5YcSDMJBUBYH3CcsHR-iTzYiSBw2iwwgnlhUMhJjXCFZi4COHS4TwENN4t3crCyWQrMCuDH6BIMrEBFRQQaH9zAE9eRiGPPNnGBzfFXQur1ooWJ81fYuQ71zIIR6RqS9LPzVYLmvCKjcVj-2~5KEkpwbKsEK-JEkAvZ6lC2dTdxvIbW0Wb3sP184blPlWq7nUzK3QaGbmDtmnF1PW5xEKSKWcHgAT~zS8pM7C-Y8-7t6j1VEhZQSP1izrsyPmX-DKXKfzif4RUL49FuiWV6giduU19jfQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Postage stamp images of the candidate lensed z\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 galaxy in field BoRG$\\_0440$-5244 in the four HST/WFC3 filters (left to right: V600, Y098, J125, H160). The images are 5.0\u00a0arcsec on each side. All cutouts are shown on the same scale.</p></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154449 id=\"26154449\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-3>2.3 Photometry of the dropout and foreground objects</h3>\r\n<div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">The candidate <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 galaxy, borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_682$|\u2060</span>, was identified in field borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-5244 (following the notation of Bradley et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). Identification of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 dropouts is made according to strict colour selection. In general, <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a07.5 galaxies are identified due to a strong break between the <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> and <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> filters, a blue or flat <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> \u2212 <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> colour and a non-detection in the optical <em>V</em><sub>600</sub> band. The selection criteria requires, <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"\" content-id=\"\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray*}\r\n&amp;&amp;{{\\rm S/N}_{V_{600}} &lt; 1.5}\\nonumber \\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{(Y_{098} - J_{125}) &gt; 1.75}\\nonumber \\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{(J_{125} - H_{160}) &lt; 0.02 + 0.15[(Y_{098} - J_{125}) - 1.75]}\\nonumber .\r\n\\end{eqnarray*} </div></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The conservative non-detection limit of 1.5\u03c3 in the <em>V</em><sub>600</sub> filter is crucial in producing a clean <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 sample (Bouwens et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). The photometry presented by Bradley et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) of the candidates analysed here gives a <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> magnitude of 25.9\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1\u00a0mag, a <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> residual of &gt;2.1\u00a0mag, and S/N after sky subtraction in <em>V</em><sub>600</sub>, <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>, <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> of \u22120.8, \u22120.5, 9.1 and 5.7, respectively. We find a <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> ellipticity for the dropout of \u03f5\u00a0=\u00a00.4\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1 tangential to the direction of the largest of the proposed lensing galaxies. The <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> half-light radius of the dropout was measured, using SE<span class=\"small-caps\">xtractor</span>, to be 0.21\u00a0arcsec (1.1\u00a0kpc at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08; not corrected for PSF broadening).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The two brighter foreground objects are identified as a single blended source (borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_647$|\u2060</span>) with <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{J_{125}}=23.41\\pm 0.02$|</span>\u00a0mag in the BoRG SE<span class=\"small-caps\">xtractor</span> catalogue. We performed fixed aperture photometry on the individual galaxies of borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_647$|</span> and found the brighter galaxy to be 1.3\u20131.5\u00a0mag brighter than the fainter galaxy in each of the filters, making the colours of the two galaxies essentially identical colours. The galaxy borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_650$|\u2060</span>, has <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{J_{125}}\\sim 24.58\\pm 0.14$|</span>\u00a0mag. The photometry of all objects is summarized in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"26154453\" scrollto-destination=\"26154453\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The photometry for the primary dropout (ID: 682), the main lensing group (ID: 647) and a nearby galaxy (ID: 650) which is potentially part of the group. The main lensing group (647) has a spectroscopically confirmed redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327. The photometric redshift probability distribution of the third object (650) is extended; however, it has a non-negligible probability of residing at the same redshift as the central galaxies.</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table><thead><tr><th>ID<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>V</em><sub>600</sub><span .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>J</em><sub>125</sub><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>H</em><sub>160</sub><span aria-hidden=\"true\" .\u00a0</span></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>682\u00a0</td><td>&gt;28.26\u00a0</td><td>&gt;28.15\u00a0</td><td>25.92\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.14\u00a0</td><td>25.75\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.19\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>647\u00a0</td><td>24.20\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.07\u00a0</td><td>23.87\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03\u00a0</td><td>23.41\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02\u00a0</td><td>23.49\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.04\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>650\u00a0</td><td>25.17\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.13\u00a0</td><td>24.87\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.05\u00a0</td><td>24.58\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.14\u00a0</td><td>24.31\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.31\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/26154453\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154454 id=\"26154454\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-4>2.4 Photometry of the candidate counter image</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In addition to the photometry already carried out by Bradley et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), we perform aperture photometry in <span class=\"small-caps\">iraf</span> on the primary and counter image to determine their flux ratio and the counter image's <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>V</em><sub>606</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> colours. To minimize contamination of the counter image photometry by the lensing group, we operate on a version of the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> images where we subtracted a scaled and PSF-matched version of the <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> data, where the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 candidate has dropped out. For this, we use <span class=\"small-caps\">isis2.2</span> (Alard <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>) to produce a convolution kernel between the images in the different bands and to match the point spread functions (PSFs). There is some residual in the subtracted images due to the foreground galaxies having intrinsically different profiles between filters. The galaxies on the whole, though, are adequately subtracted, and the residuals do not affect the photometry at the image positions. The subtracted images are shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"26154456\" scrollto-destination=\"26154456\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig3.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=3oRe~IY7UZ7PIL~DQu9Q3UineWMa5nTfEhTR9WbIvjj0pJaruzFAqqechnn6UexcbAdP7vW-t7QTXR9nRNNfrv7GShIv0xNzoAPET1K1LefrYXvEPNC4AFOOxYuE04ADNSUfuu3Z6~R1uLzrXZDau~7Hr7I-rmoe5lRHlDDA~37wfpf4hXTvGYxFvaBCzze7zucUEC257m63DXhP070jwlPx6DF4LI4UB~-xf8ZB3zl7tIa9Y6XqqT0nNPl54NcNm2On53HAASslRjSAABrcIrmiva295y6446RpmHFLaxaLOSQXtZklLqJ5G8yTqNfi~~F1sXmBVOkNnhD9HNrgeQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Normalized residuals for the subtractions of the PSF-matched Y098 image from the J125 image (left) and H160 image (right). There is a marginal detection of the counter image (S/N\u00a0\u223c\u00a02) in J125. As expected, the counter image is undetected in the H160 filter. The images are 5.0\u00a0arcsec on each side. There remains some residual of the deflector galaxy cores due to the varying light profiles of the galaxies between filters. There is a marginal detection of the counter image (S/N\u00a0\u223c\u00a02) in <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>. As expected, the counter image is undetected in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> filter. The location of the dropout objects are circled in black.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig3.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=3oRe~IY7UZ7PIL~DQu9Q3UineWMa5nTfEhTR9WbIvjj0pJaruzFAqqechnn6UexcbAdP7vW-t7QTXR9nRNNfrv7GShIv0xNzoAPET1K1LefrYXvEPNC4AFOOxYuE04ADNSUfuu3Z6~R1uLzrXZDau~7Hr7I-rmoe5lRHlDDA~37wfpf4hXTvGYxFvaBCzze7zucUEC257m63DXhP070jwlPx6DF4LI4UB~-xf8ZB3zl7tIa9Y6XqqT0nNPl54NcNm2On53HAASslRjSAABrcIrmiva295y6446RpmHFLaxaLOSQXtZklLqJ5G8yTqNfi~~F1sXmBVOkNnhD9HNrgeQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Normalized residuals for the subtractions of the PSF-matched Y098 image from the J125 image (left) and H160 image (right).
