The location of the dropout objects are circled in black.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig3.tiff\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/26154456/stv1872fig3.tiff\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig3.tiff\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"26154456\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/stv1872fig3.png?Expires=1611467343&Signature=bCR60bEWdUPwMZB4OuTain2czW1U62fVrXlm73xy-1SpzXjHZKJd3jDKOhlwHXNcnVh-jowXOcW9xHE04mbI6Obx6vZmSD5dy7HwpziJhh0BP0QRLrSt9HiT0q5RlhS2Yl1BlACiYNDNZYEXK3YRxEd2q8-apGdkgaqzEa77ReK40zBd~6bm3onKfL4CBp4kv9myq7iGc3Ga1xyuS-yHpohd6Z5Fm2l3BdkCXMgRbN-9zy1NzWllRYWITQYAY5wUD8pDNdkvk2cOhUPBRzg~kW2YHUA8PWJvdNraq~zJkGizp-f4sNduDT6Pw4th6~IvpAbIMUAJ-m91UzD~S0yUug__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=26154456&ar=1752732&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig3.tiff\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Normalized residuals for the subtractions of the PSF-matched <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> image from the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> image (left) and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> image (right). The images are 5.0\u00a0arcsec on each side. There remains some residual of the deflector galaxy cores due to the varying light profiles of the galaxies between filters. There is a marginal detection of the counter image (S/N\u00a0\u223c\u00a02) in <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>. As expected, the counter image is undetected in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> filter. The location of the dropout objects are circled in black.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Photometry is performed in a 4\u00a0pixel circular aperture (0.32\u00a0arcsec). In <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>, the integrated flux in the primary image is 1.54\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.18\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221230</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup>\u00a0Hz<sup>\u22121</sup> (consistent with the S/N = 9.1 determination in Bradley et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), and the flux in the counter image is 3.21\u00a0\u00b1\u00a01.72\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221231</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup>\u00a0Hz<sup>\u22121</sup>. The uncertainty includes both Poisson noise and background. This gives a flux ratio of 4.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a02.6, where the large error propagates from the low S/N of the counter image.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We measure a <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> colour redder than 1.2\u00a0mag and a <em>V</em><sub>606</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> colour redder than 0.5\u00a0mag for the counter image. When the <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> and <em>V</em><sub>606</sub> images are stacked, the (<em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>\u00a0+\u00a0<em>V</em><sub>606</sub>) \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> colour is redder than 1.4\u00a0mag. While BoRG is not designed to detect such faint objects, and neither of these colours satisfy the formal BoRG criteria for <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG selection, the colours are consistent with both the brighter image, and the source being at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 but beyond the limiting depths of this field.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We do not detect a signal at the location of the counter image in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> image; however, this is not surprising as the flux ratio between the primary and counter image is measured in <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> to be 4.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a02.6, and the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> primary image is detected at 5.7\u03c3, hence we only expect the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> counter image to be undetected (S/N = 1.2\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.7). Inspection of the individual flat-fielded files in <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> does not suggest that the faint counter image candidate is a detector artefact.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The non-detection in <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> is taken into account in our MCMC analysis (Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a>), as both bands are fitted simultaneously.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154461 id=\"26154461\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-5>2.5 Spectroscopy of the central foreground galaxies and dropout</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The source and foreground galaxy configuration and image flux ratios outlined in the previous sections and Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> present the exciting possibility that this system is a <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 galaxy gravitationally lensed by a foreground galaxy group. In order to further strengthen this interpretation, we obtained spectroscopic observations of the foreground galaxy group and <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG candidate. The goals of the spectroscopic measurements of the system are twofold. The first goal was to obtain spectroscopic redshifts for the two foreground galaxies (ID: 647). The second goal was to either identify emission lines, such as Ly\u00a0\u03b1, at the location of the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG candidate (ID: 682), or use the lack of emission lines to constrain its redshift in conjunction with its photometric colours (e.g. Treu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib74\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib74\" data-open=\"bib74\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In order to obtain these measurements, we carried out VLT/X-Shooter spectroscopic observations in visitor mode on 2013 August 13\u201315 (program #091.A-0053, PI Puzia). Observing conditions were excellent with seeing in the range 0.6\u20130.9\u00a0arcsec. The X-Shooter long slit (11\u00a0arcsec) was positioned to cover both the central pair of foreground deflectors (ID: 647 in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>) and the Y-dropout (ID: 682). X-Shooter provides an uninterrupted wavelength coverage in the range 300\u00a0&lt;\u00a0\u03bb\u00a0&lt;\u00a02480\u2009nm, allowing us to characterize emission lines both from the deflector and the dropouts with a single observation. A total exposure time of 6\u00a0h (3\u00a0h on target) was achieved on the source. Telluric standard stars were observed for calibration purposes throughout the duration of the observations. The data were then reduced using the European Southern Observatory (ESO) X-Shooter pipeline v.2.5.2 (Modigliani et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib43\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib43\" data-open=\"bib43\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) and the Gasgano data file organizer developed by ESO.</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=26154464 id=\"26154464\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-5-1>2.5.1 Emission lines from the foreground galaxies</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We search for emission lines at the location of the two central foreground galaxies to determine their redshift. The two galaxies have a separation of 0.7\u00a0arcsec, and the seeing of the observations was 0.6\u20130.9\u00a0arcsec, therefore the two galaxies are unresolved in the spectrum. We identify the redshifted hydrogen\u00a0\u03b1 6563\u2009\u00c5, hydrogen\u00a0\u03b2 4861\u2009\u00c5, [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] 5007 and 4959\u2009\u00c5 doublet and the [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] 3726 and 3729\u2009\u00c5 doublet emission lines at the location of the two foreground galaxies. The two-dimensional spectrum of the hydrogen\u00a0\u03b1 and [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] doublet emission lines are shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>. The observed emission lines unambiguously places the foreground galaxy pair at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327, supporting the gravitational lensing hypothesis. This redshift is at the peak of the redshift distribution for the deflectors of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a07\u20138 LBGs (Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p>                        <a id=\"26154466\" scrollto-destination=\"26154466\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 4.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig4.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=w-RjYJrBjh2LxRFF8ZGJ0YIzBk5eVLwAIdWfbvuQq1BlMv3kzSR6r3H-T9n4i3OkY-dzH7hspzOqkD5IYhHbSkpavTj0dxBmKqVcqBJJv75nmA9RVTTF3xBPKka0-3Z7KiLmvM-O4R9fyYFCo~kWZBjmw0q4ZBNSypo67O9qG34EFvDozsREmF9PdY2J41gHiys3lpRk9Kn95iJkoNUDK2KyyfQPP552TGSFWUtXjDKmGMn-D60vMR2eLuPQPz3jcGmStosD-baNXjueXDlLmO9Ji-Rzrj8YWkdh4-SLik~R~9hfCOyDVVs2f~PsIA74fRSFDsk58jrxIJqsZmf6mQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The cropped two-dimensional spectrum of the central deflector galaxies, obtained using X-Shooter on the VLT. These emission lines provide a robust spectroscopic redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327 for the deflector galaxies.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">It should be noted that there is a chance that the emission lines are coming only from the brighter foreground galaxy. However, the colours of the two central galaxies are virtually identical and we observe no emission lines at the location of the fainter galaxy elsewhere in the spectrum, leading to the likely possibility that the two galaxies are indeed a close pair at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327.</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=26154468 id=\"26154468\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-5-2>2.5.2 Constraints on the redshifts of the LBG</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Spectroscopic confirmation of high-redshift galaxies has been very difficult in the past, hence using gravitationally lensed LBGs provides the best opportunity to probe intrinsically fainter sources at high redshifts. The <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG candidate was included in our spectrum in order to search for the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emission line. The X-Shooter wavelength coverage would allow detection of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 line from a Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emitter at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a07, as well as other emission lines such is C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> (stark et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib62\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib62\" data-open=\"bib62\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015a</a>,<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib63\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib63\" data-open=\"bib63\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">b</a>). However we do not detect the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 line in the spectrum, nor do we detect any other emission lines. For an LBG residing at 7.6 \u2272 <em>z</em> \u2272 8.8 (the redshifts where there is a non-negligible probability density for this LBG), we show the 2D spectrum of the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub> dropout at the wavelengths where Ly\u00a0\u03b1, C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> could conceivably appear is shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a>. We place upper limits on the equivalent widths of these lines in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2-5-3\"></span><a href=\"#sec2-5-3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2.5.3</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"26154470\" scrollto-destination=\"26154470\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig5.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=WjPq9x7fUClrGWHTqot8WJGkdNzN8IeNTuLcziKpay~5Z~XuhaNh9VsrNxVBustAzMdUNMLeWE4QrOQCXzowrmKy-TzCtuR3FI4mkN-A1IOhRV5dNAMErz7MOArxGfFKTFskO~THioAiHfekVvblDGSHDQKfYGYyqmqpd-n-qTMXu17bfsnEP~05pi24QqJ~r3x-GjqViP7GU06asTwGp4RhsY4WGfI2vtGxAxfqSw9V3SPV-OZlk7sLN6bK1akyKjJzlP3jKOQ6mdluPd89LlqMP2BuvA~Ecy7qcSzsV-8~h9V7hGDbWorQwwIpHs1cQ~m6T5bHvBbBwmUZuOG~lg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The regions of the 2D spectrum where the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 (1216\u2009\u00c5, top), C\u00a0iv (1548\u2009\u00c5, middle), and C\u00a0iii] (1909\u2009\u00c5, bottom) emission lines could appear given the redshift distribution of the dropout. The portion of the spectrum covering the dropout falls within the green lines. No lines are detected at these wavelengths or elsewhere in the spectrum at the location of the dropout. We use these non-detections to rule out a major class of low-redshift interlopers, and constrain the equivalent widths of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1, C\u00a0iii] and C\u00a0iv emission lines. The portion of the spectrum covering the dropout falls within the green lines. No lines are detected at these wavelengths or elsewhere in the spectrum at the location of the dropout. We use these non-detections to rule out a major class of low-redshift interlopers, and constrain the equivalent widths of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1, C\u00a0iii] and C\u00a0iv emission lines. The hydrogen\u00a0\u03b2 and [O\u00a0iii] doublet emission lines from the central galaxy pair are visible in the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 detection region at 11\u2009312, 11\u2009540 and 11\u2009651\u2009\u00c5, respectively.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig5.tiff\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/26154470/stv1872fig5.tiff\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig5.tiff\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"26154470\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/stv1872fig5.png?Expires=1611467343&Signature=Lw6qfGmwd7iBPP7BX4Ijh7AZ01G1WrZSIflNhfkueLP7XGAtxAil7W5KC9Tp7Gk6TbllBRVva17xxVHXzEWEe3ommqcNb2QYEvCl5iEfYRddXlQS-m0teDdWs428riSVhapTJ5h29MfsOw7v3R~zz8UjaTSdn7JQjkZQrMnUPgX49G6uxNugcFQdtaCyxH~kXdYWSaJsrE7r6jhjdksbHwWT-I3ShS3MqybosCKqZjuMN27bbRudf~Wy~TF4Uz2Ftv4fopkbmL6WRUlxEjGPujeUpclERhigwUlVeURJvVAoWdDDjt4r-vUuKPYAG02YhD6c7ianNX7bnzTkK5JYQA__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=26154470&ar=1752732&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig5.tiff\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The regions of the 2D spectrum where the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 (1216\u2009\u00c5, top), C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> (1548\u2009\u00c5, middle), and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] (1909\u2009\u00c5, bottom) emission lines could appear given the redshift distribution of the dropout. The portion of the spectrum covering the dropout falls within the green lines. No lines are detected at these wavelengths or elsewhere in the spectrum at the location of the dropout. We use these non-detections to rule out a major class of low-redshift interlopers, and constrain the equivalent widths of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1, C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> emission lines. The hydrogen\u00a0\u03b2 and [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] doublet emission lines from the central galaxy pair are visible in the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 detection region at 11\u2009312, 11\u2009540 and 11\u2009651\u2009\u00c5, respectively.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Despite the lack of visible emission lines, the spectrum of the LBG candidate is nevertheless useful for constraining the strong lensing hypothesis since we can rule out the possibility of the source being a strong emission line contaminant. We do not observe any emission lines at the location of the dropout down to the sensitivity limit of our spectroscopic observations. While this prevents us from achieving spectroscopic confirmation, the non-detection of emission lines is important to exclude the most significant class of contaminants in samples of high-redshift LBGs. These contaminants are objects with a very weak continuum and very strong hydrogen\u00a0\u03b1, hydrogen\u00a0\u03b2 and [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] emission located at 1.3\u00a0\u2272\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0\u2272\u00a01.7, which could exhibit colours similar to those observed in the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 candidate of this paper (Atek et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We consider the noise levels of the dropout spectrum to place limits on the contribution to the observed broad-band flux from emission lines. The integrated line flux at \u03bb \u2248 1.6\u2009\u03bcm required to produce a broad-band flux of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{H_{160}}=25.75$|</span>\u00a0mag is 7.8\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221217</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup>. Assuming a simple model of an emission line with a width of 10\u2009\u00c5, the required flux density to account for all of the broad-band magnitude is 7.8\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221218</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup> \u2009\u00c5<sup>\u22121</sup>. The median noise in the spectrum in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> band is 4.6\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221219</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup> \u2009\u00c5<sup>\u22121</sup>. This allows us to rule out the presence of an emission line contributing more than <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{H_{160}}=28.6$|</span>\u00a0mag at 5\u03c3, and contributing all of the observed broad-band flux of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{H_{160}}=25.75$|</span>\u00a0mag at 70\u03c3. Similarly, the integrated line flux required to produce a broad-band flux of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{J_{125}}=25.92$|</span>\u00a0mag is 7.9\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221217</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup>, and the median noise level in the spectrum covering the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band is 1.0\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>\u221218</sup>\u00a0erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup>\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup> \u2009\u00c5<sup>\u22121</sup>. This allows us to rule out the presence of an emission line contributing more than <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{J_{125}}=27.9$|</span>\u00a0mag at 5\u03c3, and contributing the all of the observed broad-band flux of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{J_{125}}=25.92$|</span>\u00a0mag at 30\u03c3.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We calculate the likelihood that the emission lines are hidden behind sky lines or obscured by atmospheric absorption. We define the obscured part of the spectrum as the region where an emission line detected at 5\u03c3 at the median noise would be detected at less than 2\u03c3. The percentage of the spectrum covering the broad-band <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> filters obscured by sky lines or atmospheric absorption above the required level of emission lines is \u223c14\u00a0per\u00a0cent. If the dropout resides at 1.3\u00a0\u2272\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0\u2272\u00a01.7, the likelihood that both the brighter [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] emission line and hydrogen\u00a0\u03b1 line are obscured is 10\u00a0per\u00a0cent. The likelihood that the hydrogen\u00a0\u03b1 line and both of the [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] lines are obscured is 7\u00a0per\u00a0cent.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We conclude through this simple analysis that emission lines from the dropout source can contribute at most \u223c20\u00a0per\u00a0cent of the broad-band flux in <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and less than \u223c10\u00a0per\u00a0cent in <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>, therefore excluding lower redshift solutions with a faint (undetected) continuum and broad-band photometry dominated by strong emission lines with very high confidence.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">As a consistency check, we compare the required luminosity of the emission lines in the case of the dropout being a low-redshift interloper with the detected emission lines of the foreground galaxies. For emission lines to contribute the required flux in <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> for the dropout, they would need to be as bright as the observed [O\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] 4959\u2009\u00c5 line from the foreground galaxy pair, and twice as bright as the observed hydrogen\u00a0\u03b2 line, both of which are detected with high confidence (\u227310\u03c3).</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=26154476 id=\"26154476\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-5-3>2.5.3 Equivalent width constraints from the LBG spectrum</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In addition to ruling out strong emission line interlopers, the absence of emission lines allows us to place upper limits on the equivalent widths of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1, C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> emission lines for this LBG. Each of these emission lines have been observed in spectra of LBGs at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a06 previously (Ono et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib52\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib52\" data-open=\"bib52\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Finkelstein et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Oesch et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib50\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib50\" data-open=\"bib50\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Stark et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib62\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib62\" data-open=\"bib62\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015a</a>,<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib63\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib63\" data-open=\"bib63\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">b</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We investigate the limits that can be placed on the equivalent width of Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emission. We do this by assuming a half-Gaussian model of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emission line profile with a full width at half-maximum (FWHM) of 12\u2009\u00c5. We calculate the 5\u03c3 upper limit on the integrated line flux by considering the noise in the spectrum in the possible wavelength range of Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emission. The continuum flux density is computed from the broad-band photometry. The result is a median 5\u03c3 upper limit of the rest-frame equivalent width of EW<sub>0</sub>(Ly\u00a0\u03b1)\u00a0&lt;\u00a057\u2009\u00c5. We quantify the chance that Ly\u00a0\u03b1 is obscured by sky lines or atmospheric absorption in the region where we expect Ly\u00a0\u03b1 to appear. The redshift distribution for the LBG is centred on <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a08, but there is a non-negligible probability density from <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a07.6 to 8.8. Using the range of wavelengths at which Ly\u00a0\u03b1 could appear, we calculate that the chance that it has been obscured to be 14\u00a0per\u00a0cent.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We also constrain the equivalent width of C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> emission lines. For these emission lines, we assume a Gaussian emission line profile model with an FWHM of 12\u2009\u00c5. We calculate the 5\u03c3 upper limit on the integrated line flux by considering the noise in the spectrum in the possible wavelength range of C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> emission. The continuum flux density is again calculated from the broad-band photometry. The results are median 5\u03c3 upper limits for C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> emission of EW<sub>0</sub>(C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>])\u00a0&lt;\u00a025\u2009\u00c5 and EW<sub>0</sub>(C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>)\u00a0&lt;\u00a036\u2009\u00c5, respectively. We quantify the chance of the C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] and C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span> lines being obscured by sky lines or due to atmospheric absorption as 12\u00a0per\u00a0cent in both cases.</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=26154480 id=\"26154480\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-5-4>2.5.4 Photometric redshift of the third foreground galaxy</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The X-Shooter slit does not cover the third nearby foreground galaxy (ID: 650). To constrain the redshift of this source, we utilize the Bayesian photometric redshift code <span class=\"small-caps\">bpz</span> (Benitez <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>; Ben\u00edtez et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Coe et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>). The photometric redshift distribution of this source is characterized by a more extended probability distribution, peaking at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a00.3. However, there is a non-negligible peak in the likelihood distribution centred at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.3, leading to the distinct possibility that this galaxy is at the same redshift as the central objects and the broad redshift distribution is simply an effect of photometric scatter. The photometric redshift distribution for this third galaxy is shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"26154482\" scrollto-destination=\"26154482\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig6\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 6.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig6.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=GW3khDfS3Dfq4omz5JUWiIZBZFz1im3MBVXo~pO4pzmH1mqlleSSqWxpCV8mA-sxRjeKJdzfJSM1kneJCXiSfKZ6IHS4mXpq1-x4AogFPoybkpRRtVx8GObx1iGITfSHpmp15a1kgxEVJtlwCaigNc5V-Z8dBRsWqn~PWfwM4A3H1gDRhrQv3Qtp1Xd5~-EAFiXHzDbAlNPg26qiwWfsFF5BFtz9KW~Zkz9PKA-rE8eDdXGLZlu5Mb9Z8bhbETiGli9HF596qAVVQOM59RMIT-32~fw2yYy~Vh-UO7G5bxciQEqS5V8EDDeK6-reUGOBT7k-F1mkyRtmDvmTPr2m2Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The redshift probability distribution function for the third foreground galaxy (ID: 650), obtained with the photometric redshift code bpz using the Hubble Ultra Deep Field prior. The distribution is reasonably broad and peaks around z\u00a0=\u00a00.2\u20130.4; however, a non-negligible peak at z\u00a0=\u00a01.2\u20131.4 leads us to consider the distinct possibility that this object may also lie at the same redshift as the nearby z\u00a0=\u00a01.327 galaxies, forming a small group.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig6.tiff\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/26154482/stv1872fig6.tiff\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig6.tiff\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"26154482\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/stv1872fig6.png?Expires=1611467343&Signature=Gm22G30taWKiFM5Z2O~RZcyjZNiMcja2DCIsZgj72wsfqIsudOq3G0OqPjZMg39mPF8YtsiCkzF1t2uQBVY4iW5Kvv47AleGYqj05~pPZND61pA1SxhgFc-3v0UYHWMwPaugd4MeKdWyV1H6545OWHeX7cj~FRFKNXtVXnZ9kbI2zMyymZOiOuW1AfH1fgX3DGk~b966W7T5Oqu2CS908GeCuLU2inLZ0HQt~BHHKKsrdLAYABxRZkKkFM9NPhRPLnNSpFBlAx3dVyeC6NXDRwl5eHbMSdF2qR02uNzozqn9TY81SYG7a3ePHzLCxE9jreS8fE-K~agbQAadvOe3Cg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=26154482&ar=1752732&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig6.tiff\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The redshift probability distribution function for the third foreground galaxy (ID: 650), obtained with the photometric redshift code <span class=\"small-caps\">bpz</span> using the <em>Hubble Ultra Deep Field</em> prior. The distribution is reasonably broad and peaks around <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.2\u20130.4; however, a non-negligible peak at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.2\u20131.4 leads us to consider the distinct possibility that this object may also lie at the same redshift as the nearby <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327 galaxies, forming a small group.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig6\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 6.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig6.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=GW3khDfS3Dfq4omz5JUWiIZBZFz1im3MBVXo~pO4pzmH1mqlleSSqWxpCV8mA-sxRjeKJdzfJSM1kneJCXiSfKZ6IHS4mXpq1-x4AogFPoybkpRRtVx8GObx1iGITfSHpmp15a1kgxEVJtlwCaigNc5V-Z8dBRsWqn~PWfwM4A3H1gDRhrQv3Qtp1Xd5~-EAFiXHzDbAlNPg26qiwWfsFF5BFtz9KW~Zkz9PKA-rE8eDdXGLZlu5Mb9Z8bhbETiGli9HF596qAVVQOM59RMIT-32~fw2yYy~Vh-UO7G5bxciQEqS5V8EDDeK6-reUGOBT7k-F1mkyRtmDvmTPr2m2Q__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The redshift probability distribution function for the third foreground galaxy (ID: 650), obtained with the photometric redshift code bpz using the Hubble Ultra Deep Field prior. The distribution is reasonably broad and peaks around z\u00a0=\u00a00.2\u20130.4; however, a non-negligible peak at z\u00a0=\u00a01.2\u20131.4 leads us to consider the distinct possibility that this object may also lie at the same redshift as the nearby z\u00a0=\u00a01.327 galaxies, forming a small group.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig6.tiff\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/26154482/stv1872fig6.tiff\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig6.tiff\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"26154482\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/stv1872fig6.png?Expires=1611467343&Signature=Gm22G30taWKiFM5Z2O~RZcyjZNiMcja2DCIsZgj72wsfqIsudOq3G0OqPjZMg39mPF8YtsiCkzF1t2uQBVY4iW5Kvv47AleGYqj05~pPZND61pA1SxhgFc-3v0UYHWMwPaugd4MeKdWyV1H6545OWHeX7cj~FRFKNXtVXnZ9kbI2zMyymZOiOuW1AfH1fgX3DGk~b966W7T5Oqu2CS908GeCuLU2inLZ0HQt~BHHKKsrdLAYABxRZkKkFM9NPhRPLnNSpFBlAx3dVyeC6NXDRwl5eHbMSdF2qR02uNzozqn9TY81SYG7a3ePHzLCxE9jreS8fE-K~agbQAadvOe3Cg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=26154482&ar=1752732&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig6.tiff\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The redshift probability distribution function for the third foreground galaxy (ID: 650), obtained with the photometric redshift code <span class=\"small-caps\">bpz</span> using the <em>Hubble Ultra Deep Field</em> prior. The distribution is reasonably broad and peaks around <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.2\u20130.4; however, a non-negligible peak at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.2\u20131.4 leads us to consider the distinct possibility that this object may also lie at the same redshift as the nearby <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327 galaxies, forming a small group.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The possibility that the third foreground galaxy is part of the group with the two galaxies at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327 supports a larger total dark matter (DM) mass of the deflector. However, the DM mass required for strong lensing in our lens modelling of the system (see Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a>) is not ruled out if this additional galaxy is not part of the group. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a>, we model the system with only a single mass distribution centred on the centre-of-light of the spectroscopically confirmed galaxy pair, thereby assuming it resides at the centre of the halo of the group.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=26154484 id=\"26154484\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 MEASUREMENT OF LENS AND SOURCE PROPERTIES USING AN MCMC BAYESIAN INFERENCE</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In this section, we model the observed configuration using a singular isothermal ellipsoid (SIE) mass distribution for the foreground group of galaxies, centred at the centre of light of the spectroscopically confirmed galaxy pair, and a S\u00e9rsic brightness profile for the source. We have implemented the Metropolis algorithm in an MCMC analysis to find the posterior probability distribution function (posterior pdf) of source and deflector parameters within a Bayesian framework.</p><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Our deflector mass model consists of an SIE, which is a generalization of the singular isothermal sphere, and is a commonly used parametrization of the mass distribution of a lensing galaxy (Keeton <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib34\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib34\" data-open=\"bib34\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001a</a>). The SIE is the simplest mass model that provides an adequate representation of the mass distribution of massive ellipticals (Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib37\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib37\" data-open=\"bib37\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1995</a>; Treu &amp; Koopmans <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib72\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib72\" data-open=\"bib72\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Koopmans et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>; Treu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib70\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib70\" data-open=\"bib70\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>). We adopt the definitions of the Einstein radius, ellipticity and position angle as described by Keeton (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib34\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib34\" data-open=\"bib34\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001a</a>). The surface mass density, \u03ba, in units of critical density, is defined by <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ1\" content-id=\"equ1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\kappa = \\frac{1}{2}\\frac{\\theta _{{\\rm ER}}}{\\sqrt{(1-\\epsilon )x^{2} + (1+\\epsilon )y^{2}}},\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(1)</span></div>where \u03b8<sub>ER</sub> is the Einstein radius, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\epsilon = \\frac{1-q^{2}}{1+q^{2}}$|</span> and <em>q</em> is the axis ratio of the ellipsoid. According to this definition the Einstein radius is defined along the intermediate axis of the ellipsoid. The Einstein radius is then related to the velocity dispersion of the SIE profile by <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ2\" content-id=\"equ2\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\theta _{{\\rm ER}} = 4 \\pi (\\frac{\\sigma _{\\star }}{c})^{2} \\frac{D_{\\rm {LS}}}{D_{\\rm {S}}},\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(2)</span></div>where \u03c3<sub>\u22c6</sub> is the line-of-sight stellar velocity dispersion, <em>D</em><sub>S</sub> is the angular diameter distance from the observer to the source and <em>D</em><sub>LS</sub> is the angular diameter distance from the deflector to the source. The centre of the SIE is fixed to coincide with the centre of light of the central galaxy pair. The deflector model therefore has three free parameters: Einstein radius (as a proxy for velocity dispersion/mass, and redshift), ellipticity and position angle.</div><p class=\"chapter-para\">For the source surface brightness distribution, we adopt the S\u00e9rsic profile (S\u00e9rsic <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib59\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib59\" data-open=\"bib59\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1963</a>). The source is defined by six free parameters: the S\u00e9rsic index, the effective radius, flux, <em>x</em>-position, <em>y</em>-position, ellipticity and position angle. This gives a total of 10 parameters for the deflector-source gravitational lens model.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154488 id=\"26154488\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3-1>3.1 The MCMC method and code</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We wrote an MCMC sampler in <span class=\"small-caps\">python</span> using the Metropolis algorithm. The code compares the BoRG data with surface brightness models of the image plane produced using <span class=\"small-caps\">gravlens</span> (Keeton <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001b</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The code follows a standard MCMC process. The log-likelihood is <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\frac{1}{2}\\chi ^{2}$|\u2060</span>, where <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\chi ^{2} = \\sum (\\frac{\\rm {model}_{i} - \\rm {data}_{i}}{\\sigma _{i}})^{2}$|\u2060</span>, the data are the WFC3 data in <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> and <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>, and the model is the PSF-convolved image plane. We use uniform priors on all parameters. As lensing is achromatic, the only difference between the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> model and the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> model comes from the PSFs and the noise model. Hence, the log-likelihood is calculated for the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> and <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> independently and summed to generate a total log-likelihood for a given model.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154491 id=\"26154491\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3-2>3.2 MCMC lens modelling</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We run the MCMC code with the 10 parameters described above. The data are cropped WFC3 FITS files in <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>, along with oversampled PSFs and rms maps. The code allows for oversampled PSFs by oversampling the image plane equivalently. The step size is optimized to deliver a success rate of 1/3. As is standard, we discard the MCMC burn in. We find well-constrained posterior pdf for each source and lens parameter.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The inferred parameters from the MCMC analysis are presented in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. A deflector with an Einstein radius of 1.49\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03\u00a0arcsec and ellipticity <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\epsilon =0.70^{+0.05}_{-0.11}$|</span> at <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$-15.3^{+2.7}_{-2.0}$|</span> \u00b0 east of north is favoured by the data. The source has a S\u00e9rsic index of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$n=0.92^{+0.24}_{-0.16}$|</span> and a major axis half-light radius of 0.7\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.1kpc (in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a> we use SE<span class=\"small-caps\">xtractor</span> to determine the circularized half-light radius for consistency with the literature). The apparent magnitude of the source would be <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$m_{J_{125}}=27.5\\pm 0.1$|</span>\u00a0mag if observed without magnification. The magnification at the location of the primary image is \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a04.3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2. The total magnification is \u03bc\u00a0=\u00a05.2\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.3. The lens model based on the median of the posterior of each parameter is presented in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig7\" data-open=\"fig7\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">7</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"26154494\" scrollto-destination=\"26154494\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig7\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 7.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig7.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=bBUxepSPQt4g1-djgZmkFdpNzA~ljaVKX1jdclCiN-weuWECuP9oSfzO2jG9gvnsxYLJWniEZbO0K1XDDPi4mqXw-bfrvZVEwaotZ6BtLtVjZHTOY5hbANe~LNPQZGPWcic6sTCrqmLmoMhhfC6SU~ASgSgdismN5qzTChg4q2OjNJYn~fgj0mgy5B4vMdvcxhP9yqSrHnQ1ALOzZFWXv07hPTgpLJkRZIeoqC9QmI--eKw2vcXkqoukw2tH6z69TwG9RfsV3bogRrSN1GJMTp~XCr4nHkHGm~1MUWZ1sGvVt051anPlL~xIQn6JrCFbNrgV91sZc~Mdk0XWXrJQTA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The lens model with parameters at the median of their MCMC distribution. js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/26154495\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The source model is presented in the left-hand panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig8\" data-open=\"fig8\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">8</a> at a finer pixel scale than the data as lensing allows us to recover more spatial information than if the source was not lensed. We also reconstruct the source in the median lens model using <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\tt LENSVIEW}$|</span> (Wayth &amp; Webster <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib78\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib78\" data-open=\"bib78\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>). <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\tt LENSVIEW}$|</span> creates a mapping matrix for a given lens model which reverse maps image plane pixels to the source plane. We do this independently for the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> images. The <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\tt LENSVIEW}$|</span> reconstructions are shown in the centre and right-hand panels of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig8\" data-open=\"fig8\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">8</a> and agree well with the MCMC results.</p>                        <a id=\"26154497\" scrollto-destination=\"26154497\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig8\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 8.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig8.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=WaHuq36jVcgttW3J3HeNM~Cyv-WvGX14fKZWin9uzm-1BPSDvj2eWjQt0FGSaN8b0TwiM92pQBdiw3h4daAfA16B7jKn3bgi06r7qqlEQDpf2sO1D5jRueUaEI1-UmaWhR7XCSgmgPG2vbym2HmSe-f-pKkfN20ZDoS~v5rluWTVV-AIjcSUXWiFdDZInXMX9waJEwzOCWmusb2Q8f3el~EPlfgk0XT8Hl66hqESwowxClXml1S5hHpGzl6ZF3C8yMCjx4Dt7LrWF7HJYFXBsW65pw9oNWIn-JHE-~XUJaWyXf8duELmw2EDo9iRdAV04KYHJytD51SGQr~DlSFvPg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Left: the MCMC recovered source. Centre: the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\tt LENSVIEW}$|</span> reconstruction. Right: the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\tt LENSVIEW}$|</span> reconstruction. As gravitational lensing magnifies surface area while preserving surface brightness, we can recover spatial information of the source with more detail than if it was not magnified. We sample the source plane at a pixel scale 4\u00a0times finer than the data. These sources have not been convolved with the <em>HST</em> WFC3 PSF. All three panels are 1.2\u00a0arcsec on each side and shown on the same scale.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">This model predicts a flux ratio of the two images of 4.92, which is consistent with the observed value of 4.8\u00a0\u00b1\u00a02.6. We did not impose an informative prior on the flux ratio, so all values are formally allowed in the model and deemed equally likely. Hence, a consistent predicted flux ratio with the measured flux ratio in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2-4\"></span><a href=\"#sec2-4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2.4</a> supports the reality of the counter image at its observed location.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">To investigate how constraining the marginal detection of the counter image is in the model, we run the MCMC code with the pixels at the location of the counter image masked. We find that in the absence of the counter image, the model is no longer well constrained and there is a degeneracy between the Einstein radius of the foreground galaxies, and the source position and magnification. This occurs because we place no informative priors on the Einstein radius and orientation of the foreground galaxies, hence massless galaxies and no magnification of the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG is considered equally as likely as intermediate or strong magnification of the source. In order to constrain the magnification of the source in the absence of the counter image, we place a prior on the velocity dispersion of the foreground galaxies using the Faber\u2013Jackson relation of Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). Using this prior, we place a 1\u03c3 lower limit on the magnification of \u03bc\u00a0\u2265\u00a01.38 when masking the counter image pixels.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=26154500 id=\"26154500\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 SOURCE MORPHOLOGY</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In this section, we compare the predicted source parameters with other <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 galaxies from the literature. The intrinsic source profile recovered in our MCMC analysis, and independently using <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\tt LENSVIEW}$|</span> on the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> data, is presented in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig8\" data-open=\"fig8\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">8</a>. We use SE<span class=\"small-caps\">xtractor</span> on the intrinsic sources to determine their intrinsic effective radii. The effective radius definition is not unique in the literature. For consistency with previous work on galaxy sizes at high redshift (Grazian et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), we use SE<span class=\"small-caps\">xtractor</span> to determine the effective radius, which uses concentric circular aperture measurements. In contrast, the effective radius value found in the MCMC analysis is defined along the major axis of the S\u00e9rsic profile, which will vary by a factor of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\sqrt{q}$|\u2060</span>, where <em>q</em> is the axis ratio. The intrinsic effective radii of the source, recovered in the MCMC analysis and <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\tt LENSVIEW}$|\u2060</span>, are presented in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl3\" data-open=\"tbl3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>, and are consistent with the results of Oesch et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>), who found the average intrinsic size of a <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG to be \u223c0.5kpc.</p>                        <a id=\"26154502\" scrollto-destination=\"26154502\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl3\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl3\" data-id=\"tbl3\"><span class=\"label\">Table 3.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The intrinsic and WFC3 observed effective radii of the source recovered in the multiband MCMC analysis, and reconstructed independently for each band using <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\tt LENSVIEW}$|\u2060</span>. The intrinsic values are the source sizes once corrected for PSF-broadening, while the observed sizes include the effect of PSF-broadening.</p></div> </div><div LENSVIEW}$|</span>\u00a0</td><td>0.10\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.02\u00a0</td><td>0.50\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.09\u00a0</td><td>0.17\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.03\u00a0</td><td>0.85\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.16\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/26154502\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">PSF broadening affects the measurement of effective radii. To first approximation, <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ3\" content-id=\"equ3\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\nr^{\\rm {obs}}_{{\\rm e}}= \\sqrt{r^{\\rm {intr}^{2}}_{\\rm {e}} + r^{2}_{\\rm {PSF}}},\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(3)</span></div>where <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$r^{\\rm {obs}}_{\\rm {e}}$|</span> is the observed effective radius, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$r^{\\rm {intr}}_{\\rm {e}}$|</span> is the intrinsic effective radius and <em>r</em><sub>PSF</sub> is the FWHM of the PSF. Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl3\" data-open=\"tbl3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a> summarizes the measurements of the observed size.</div><p class=\"chapter-para\">We compare our results with the size\u2013luminosity relation measured at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a07 by Grazian et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig9\" data-open=\"fig9\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">9</a>. We account for an expected approximate scaling of the galaxy radius with redshift as 1/(1\u00a0+\u00a0<em>z</em>), in line with the study by Oesch et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>), who constrained the redshift evolution of the scalelength of galactic discs in the Hubble Ultra Deep Field, and theoretical predictions by Wyithe &amp; Loeb (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib81\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib81\" data-open=\"bib81\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). We find that the recovered properties of our source are consistent with the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a07 sample presented in that work. The <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|${\\tt LENSVIEW}$|</span> reconstruction and the source recovered in the MCMC analysis are plotted in red in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig9\" data-open=\"fig9\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">9</a>. We also plot the size and luminosity of the primary image if it has not been lensed and find that the galaxy would not be an outlier on the relation.</p>                        <a id=\"26154505\" scrollto-destination=\"26154505\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig9\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 9.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig9.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=BanpGcHzjOTYw6KwYTj-Am-xMYbWfJ-J-8ThR23NNnoGJdv922hVTdxvMA1-JxH0LLWTKOM9zuVtiZbwk5WZisk3Kg1J~AEqbKmV7dXLWbfTY6fEPKme7cUrZZD5V7~fF2EeJdlR3V9c6iWkKOLIAkYw1JJ37HGLODVEnj5CPGJfxUD0MhvFGYrus3YmIBeI4A0Db156vkPtCWXfH5XzZfNlXxFpLG-Y6wzFPCAoWkJyyvqexxS8FS-7oEVlQTqLhwF12UY2KThWA2KrbHSPoaJ9vLA4uBdNpzEqsseLoPoAOaDTCPTN62aWBBvjyVM8Ec~GJJEIiomP0iFtNWku4g__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Size versus luminosity relation for the Y098-dropout source under the lensing scenario, as recovered from our MCMC analysis and as reconstructed with ${\\tt LENSVIEW}$ (red, mJ\u00a0=\u00a027.5\u00a0mag). The blue point (<em>m</em><sub><em>J</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a025.9\u00a0mag) shows the same measurement but assuming that no lensing magnification is present. Both scenarios are consistent with the size\u2013luminosity relation measured by Grazian et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a07, and scaled to <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 assuming <em>r</em>(<em>z</em>)\u2009\u221d\u20091/(1\u00a0+\u00a0<em>z</em>) (Oesch et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>; Wyithe &amp; Loeb <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib81\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib81\" data-open=\"bib81\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). The change in distance modulus from <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a07 to 8 is accounted for.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Additionally, we compare our results with the size\u2013luminosity relations of Shibuya, Ouchi &amp; Harikane (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib60\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib60\" data-open=\"bib60\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) and Curtis-Lake et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Shibuya et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib60\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib60\" data-open=\"bib60\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) find the size of \u223c<em>L</em><sub>\u22c6</sub> LBGs at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 to be <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$0.419^{+1.981}_{-0.262}$|</span>\u2009kpc, consistent with the LBG if it has not been significantly magnified, and the size of LBGs two magnitudes fainter to be <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$0.243^{+0.225}_{-0.068}$|</span>\u2009kpc, consistent with the size of the LBG under the strong lensing hypothesis. We also find that the size of the LBG under the lensing hypothesis is consistent with the sizes of the <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBGs in Curtis-Lake et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>), but also consistent with the absence of lensing due to the scatter in the relation. Thus, the size of the <em>Y</em><sub>098</sub>-dropout is consistent with literature data whether the lensing hypothesis is true or not.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=26154507 id=\"26154507\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 DEFLECTOR MASS-TO-LIGHT RATIO</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Strong gravitational lensing offers a direct and uniquely precise measurement of the deflector mass distribution. Lensing constraints are free from assumptions of a system's dynamical properties which is critical in other direct measurements of a system's mass (Cappellari et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>). Under the assumption that we are, in fact, observing a lens system as described in this paper, we can measure the mass of a <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327 group and its associated massive galaxies with unprecedented precision. We measure the mass enclosed within the Einstein radius of the deflector system, as well as the total mass enclosed within the effective radius of the brighter galaxy of the spectroscopically confirmed deflector.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">To calculate the mass enclosed by the Einstein radius, we integrate the SIE mass distribution over the Einstein radius of 1.49\u00a0arcsec. We find the mass within the effective radius by fitting a de Vaucouleurs profile to the main deflector galaxy using <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> to determine its effective radius, <em>r</em><sub>e</sub>, and its de Vaucouleurs luminosity, <em>L</em><sub>deVauc</sub>. The mass within the effective radius is then calculated by integrating the SIE mass distribution over <em>r</em><sub>e</sub>. It should be noted that the effective radius of the de Vaucouleurs profile is defined by <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> along the major axis. For consistency with the mass measurement within the Einstein radius, we integrate the mass over the effective radius defined along the intermediate axis.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Calculating the physical masses and intrinsic luminosities of the deflector galaxies requires knowledge of the source and deflector redshifts. We consider the uncertainty in the spectroscopic redshift of the main deflector to be negligible compared to the uncertainty in the source LBG's redshift, and other systematic errors. The non-negligible range for the redshift PDF of the source is 7.6 \u2272 <em>z</em> \u2272 8.8, and the uncertainty on the brighter galaxy effective radius to be 20\u00a0per\u00a0cent in order to account for systematic errors which dominate the formal statistical errors provided by <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span>. The centre of the deflector is fixed in the MCMC analysis, but we account for uncertainty in its location when calculating the physical mass enclosed within the effective radius of the brighter galaxy. We also include errors on the solar luminosity, <em>K</em>-correction, systematics in the photometry and random errors in the MCMC analysis. The resulting values for measured quantities are quoted at their median and the resulting errors on the derived quantities are quoted and plotted at the 68\u00a0per\u00a0cent confidence limit.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The mass enclosed within the Einstein radius of 1.49\u00a0arcsec of the SIE mass distribution is 9.62\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.31\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>11</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>. Photometry of the luminous matter enclosed within the Einstein radius is listed in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>. We apply the distance modulus out to <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.327 and a <em>K</em>-correction using single stellar populations models with ages in the range 1\u20132\u00a0Gyr to convert the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> magnitude to the rest-frame <em>B</em>-band magnitude. We note that the redshifted <em>B</em> band is very close to the observed <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and therefore the <em>K</em>-correction is fairly robust with respect to changes in the assumed spectral energy distribution, resulting in a negligible additional uncertainty. Combining these measurements, we find a total mass-to-light ratio within the Einstein radius of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$M/L_{B}=38.8^{+4.2}_{-3.6} \\,\\mathrm{M}_{{\\odot }}/\\mathrm{L}_{{\\odot }}$|\u2060</span>. This suggests that DM dominates the mass of the deflector and supports the argument that the deflector is a group. The Einstein radius is \u223c20\u00a0times as large as the <em>r</em><sub>e</sub> of the central deflector galaxy which is consistent with a mass distribution dominated by DM.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">To obtain the stellar mass-to-light ratio of the brighter central deflector, we calculate the lensing mass within its effective radius, <em>r</em><sub>e</sub>, and account for the DM fraction as follows. We use <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> to fit a de Vaucouleurs profile to the main deflector galaxy. We find it to have circularized <em>r</em><sub>e</sub> = 0.072 \u00b1 0.014\u00a0arcsec, and a magnitude of <em>m</em><sub>deVauc</sub> = 23.55 \u00b1 0.1\u00a0mag. We find the circular effective radius to be <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$0.62^{+0.14}_{-0.13}$|</span>\u2009kpc, making the galaxy very compact and less luminous than the most massive galaxies at comparable redshift (Damjanov et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>). Within this galaxy's effective radius the SIE mass distribution has a mass of 4.3\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.3\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>10</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>. The left-hand panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig10\" data-open=\"fig10\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">10</a> shows this galaxy's stellar mass and effective radius in comparison with the sample of ellipticals at 1\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a01.5 from Newman et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>).</p>                        <a id=\"26154513\" scrollto-destination=\"26154513\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig10\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 10.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig10.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=IJ2zasuAAC~zCM-Qwg8mmLi8Tzx-l0XK~jrsyVaCYapYtpzjgmax8UoHH3e11OH5rDhlSnRt18flXEnn0IjyfdYU7yTOqD2CSpiBtjfQDaTT2ZCXClq6lXNuNSy5WBUsqrZ7G7TV8lgfNMMijrS3fS5FFS1YdLxQwCDcQMtIC~tWgjV3f0T6LIH7-EMhYjGcESeqfEzeXSPaIzIeED6BY8xeOkSjKe9suTJvVuexfEC6H8vqPDJh48-ryqUcU0KdguhVQF2NUKNJInw6jUWQh~DWPHfBs0sHtbTrBm0MxZCIcer1OYM17EvFq8O0lKaOTmLqwplfBmTQiLChwDroyQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Left: the size\u2013mass relation at 1\u00a0&lt;\u00a0z\u00a0&lt;\u00a01.5. The open squares show the measured stellar masses from spectral synthesis models of multicolour photometry (Newman et\u00a0al. 2012). Our lens candidate (red point) falls on the relation, using our lensing-based estimate of the stellar mass presented in this work. Right: cosmic evolution of the stellar mass-to-light ratio based on gravitational lenses at lower redshift (Treu &amp; Koopmans 2004), the evolution of the Fundamental Plane measured out to z\u00a0\u223c\u00a01.2 (Treu et\u00a0al. 2002). The red point represents the candidate lens presented in this paper.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig10.tiff\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/26154513/stv1872fig10.tiff\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig10.tiff\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"26154513\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/stv1872fig10.png?Expires=1611467343&Signature=K8XnmlZtVtTpAVv7FAec6rmuBXDQaPRKy5ux0Paaaj16xGWlGe9qtYhWD6aeG02lPmu0-xrFBuFz2BVHVR85lEvY1iDgGVvRpD9cjhq2P0M1VKziStQOmDE1S9EPMppYIpT4du2940J2q2-uh2j0YewUAnr3IMOFP49a2iIvLpDHl2oBhhK88vaTW3Pv0ZQp3dLq6b~OYEDwsgMM~KRWLBJya-x5I7mT5Bge7YGd8HMkNcx24ktoD9Q2OtbCPk1j7g8Ym9LZosL1~vzeTSBY2rr0Y~y3msFAmCCINtJiGqAFQQaR7Cmdk20HsIe7lB16SQ1WQn37AyZHkzUD4f2xWg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=26154513&ar=1752732&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv1872fig10.tiff\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Left: the size\u2013mass relation at 1\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a01.5. The open squares show the measured stellar masses from spectral synthesis models of multicolour photometry (Newman et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). Our lens candidate (red point) falls on the relation, using our lensing-based estimate of the stellar mass presented in this work. Right: cosmic evolution of the stellar mass-to-light ratio based on gravitational lenses at lower redshift (Treu &amp; Koopmans <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib72\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib72\" data-open=\"bib72\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>), the evolution of the Fundamental Plane measured out to <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a01.2 (Treu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib73\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib73\" data-open=\"bib73\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>). The red point represents the candidate lens presented in this paper.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">We apply the distance modulus and <em>K</em>-correction to convert the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> magnitude to the rest-frame <em>B</em>-band magnitude. We find a mass-to-light ratio within the effective radius of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$M/L_{B} = 3.5^{+1.2}_{-0.9} \\,\\mathrm{M}_{{\\odot }}/\\mathrm{L}_{{\\odot }}$|\u2060</span>. Adopting the average DM fraction of 1/3 found for SLACS systems of this mass (Treu &amp; Koopmans <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib72\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib72\" data-open=\"bib72\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>; Auger et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010a</a>), we obtain a stellar mass-to-light ratio of <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$M_{\\star }/L_B=2.3^{+0.8}_{-0.6} \\,\\mathrm{M}_{{\\odot }}/\\mathrm{L}_{{\\odot }}$|\u2060</span>. We find that the central deflecting galaxy is consistent in size and mass with compact, massive galaxies observed at similar redshifts (so-called red nuggets) (Daddi et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2005</a>; Van Dokkum et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib76\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib76\" data-open=\"bib76\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Damjanov et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>; Newman et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). The right-hand panel of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig10\" data-open=\"fig10\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">10</a> compares our measurement of the stellar mass-to-light ratio to previous measurements of the cosmic evolution of the stellar mass-to-light ratio obtained with lensing at lower redshifts (Treu &amp; Koopmans <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib72\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib72\" data-open=\"bib72\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>) and via the evolution of the Fundamental Plane out to <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a01.2 (Treu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib73\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib73\" data-open=\"bib73\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>).</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=26154515 id=\"26154515\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6>6 DISCUSSION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We have analysed what appears to be a case of gravitational lensing of a <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG found in the BoRG survey. In the event that this source has been strongly lensed, we find the empirical lensed fraction of the galaxies detected at 8\u03c3 in BoRG to be 10\u00a0per\u00a0cent. This value is in agreement with the observed fraction of strongly lensed LBGs brighter than <em>M</em><sub>\u22c6</sub> in the Bouwens et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) sample at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a07 (Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) of \u223c6\u00a0per\u00a0cent, the value predicted for BoRG fields by Mason et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) of 3\u201315\u00a0per\u00a0cent, and the value predicted by Wyithe et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib82\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib82\" data-open=\"bib82\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>) of \u223c10\u00a0per\u00a0cent for a sample with a flux limit <em>M</em>\u00a0\u2272\u00a0<em>M</em><sub>\u22c6</sub>, such as the ten 8\u03c3 LBGs investigated here. We discuss the supporting evidence for this hypothesis in this section.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154517 id=\"26154517\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6-1>6.1 Previous studies of the lensed fraction of high-<em>z</em> LBGs</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">A study of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a07\u20138 LBGs in the XDF and Cosmic Assembly Near-infrared Deep Extragalactic Survey blank fields found the strongly lensed fraction of LBGs brighter than <em>M</em><sub>\u22c6</sub> to be \u223c6\u00a0per\u00a0cent (Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). In a separate study by (Mason et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), the strongly lensed fraction in the BoRG fields is estimated at 3\u201315\u00a0per\u00a0cent. These studies were based on the work by Wyithe et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib82\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib82\" data-open=\"bib82\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>), who predicted a strongly lensed fraction of 10\u00a0per\u00a0cent for LBGs at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08. These studies lead to the expectation that \u22481 of the ten high-S/N LBGs, which are all approximately <em>M</em><sub>\u22c6</sub> or brighter, in the BoRG sample will show evidence for strong gravitational lensing.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=26154519 id=\"26154519\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6-2>6.2 Proximity to bright foreground objects</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 LBG we have identified as a good candidate for being strongly gravitationally lensed, borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_682$|\u2060</span>, is observed in close proximity to multiple bright foreground objects, so there is a considerably enhanced chance of strong lensing for this LBG. Analysis of the CANDELS fields from Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) shows that random source positions observed within \u223c1.8\u00a0arcsec of a foreground galaxy with <em>M</em><sub><em>B</em></sub>\u00a0&lt;\u00a0\u221220\u00a0mag have a greatly enhanced likelihood of strong lensing over all random source positions. This analysis shows that the fraction of 50 000 random source positions found to be projected nearby to bright foreground objects is low (2\u00a0per\u00a0cent of all random source positions are observed within 2.0\u00a0arcsec of a bright foreground galaxy). But of the 2\u00a0per\u00a0cent which are projected within 2.0\u00a0arcsec, \u223c20\u00a0per\u00a0cent will have been strongly gravitationally lensed.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig11\" data-open=\"fig11\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">11</a> shows the likelihood of a random line of sight being observed within \u03b8<sub>sep</sub> of a foreground galaxy with <em>M</em><sub><em>B</em></sub>\u00a0&lt;\u00a0\u221220 (solid black), and the likelihood of strong lensing as a function of \u03b8<sub>sep</sub>.<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>1</sup></a> An object being observed within 1.8\u00a0arcsec of a bright foreground objects implies that it has a 23\u00a0per\u00a0cent chance of being strongly lensed. The probability of strong lensing is even more enhanced for objects observed around brighter objects (e.g. <em>M</em><sub><em>B</em></sub>\u00a0&lt;\u00a0\u221220.5\u00a0mag), giving a likelihood of lensing of \u223c30\u00a0per\u00a0cent at a separation of \u03b8<sub>sep</sub> = 1.8 arcsec. The central galaxy pair (identified as a single foreground object), borg<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\_0440$|</span>-<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5244\\_647$|\u2060</span>, has an absolute magnitude of <em>M</em><sub><em>B</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a0\u221220.5\u00a0mag.</p>                        <a id=\"26154522\" scrollto-destination=\"26154522\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig11\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 11.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/453/3/10.1093/mnras/stv1872/2/m_stv1872fig11.png?Expires=1611467343&amp;Signature=WlVlsLKf05ZwtEZjfI0zWrkLtrbU-lltRNx7TKzoVKNZsnK-9Z5MoXt8kUWOpMmaGBJ48LZHg2efM7r2S3OY4SPgv2ttNu3RJKkkMGoPgR4JrkWovOWyJmECVlm0j1fGJI3Lckei701DkLOakXKPXOW7hPsb3zDvfQFn2seGV1SKvnK5~K0cwtA7oZipoBMuL9dnC1RCeWajE38WT-abrhRL3btQzAWiH~twjQxEr0yesV2MvLunh7Be~78i2xTnN~wibHFPhdVbFtblONb4TBY6UVU4ZM1B2WIst~bujpEw~8Fk1LIhwiSs9d5VELW2yJ8WP0MT~JKkiRGK8CAkdg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The probability of observing a random z\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 source within \u03b8sep of a foreground galaxy with MB\u00a0&lt;\u00a0\u221220\u00a0mag (solid black), and the likelihood of strong lensing, P(\u03bc\u00a0&gt;\u00a02), of random lines of sight observed within \u03b8sep of a foreground galaxy with MB\u00a0&lt;\u00a0\u221220\u00a0mag (dashed blue) in GOODS-N and GOODS-S using the model of Barone-Nugent et\u00a0al.
